## 11. Kammakkhandhakaṃ - The Section on Action

### 1. Tajjanīyakammaṃ - The Act of Censure ^1

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^1|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.1" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


1. Tena samayena buddho bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca [alamatthatarā ca (syā. ka.)]. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vakkhanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattantī’’ti.

1. At that time the Blessed One was dwelling at Sāvatthī in Jeta's Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika's Park. Now at that time the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks were themselves quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha. And approaching those other monks who were quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, they said: "Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter him with all your might. You are wiser, more discerning, more learned, and more capable than him. Do not be afraid of him. We will be on your side." Thus, disputes that had not arisen came to arise, and those that had arisen increased and expanded. Those monks who were of few desires... complained, criticised, and spread it about, saying: "How can the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks, being themselves quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, approach those other monks who were quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, and say: 'Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter him with all your might. You are wiser, more discerning, more learned, and more capable than him. Do not be afraid of him. We will be on your side.' Thus, disputes that had not arisen come to arise, and those that had arisen increase and expand?"

2. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattantī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, bhikkhave, tesaṃ moghapurisānaṃ ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vakkhanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti? Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya pasannānaṃ vā bhiyyobhāvāya. Atha khvetaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānañceva appasādāya pasannānañca ekaccānaṃ aññathattāyā’’ti.

2. Then those monks informed the Blessed One about this matter. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and on this ground, had the Bhikkhu Saṅgha convened, and he questioned the monks: "Is it true, monks, that the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks are themselves quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, and that they approach those other monks who are quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, saying: 'Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter him with all your might. You are wiser, more discerning, more learned, and more capable than him. Do not be afraid of him. We will be on your side.' Thus, disputes that had not arisen came to arise, and those that had arisen increased and expanded?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked them: "It is unsuitable, monks, for these foolish men, improper, unbecoming, unworthy of a recluse, unallowable, and should not be done. How can these foolish men, monks, being themselves quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, approach those other monks who are quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, given to brawls, and makers of issues in the Saṅgha, and say: 'Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter him with all your might. You are wiser, more discerning, more learned, and more capable than him. Do not be afraid of him. We will be on your side.' Thus, disputes that had not arisen came to arise, and those that had arisen increased and expanded? This, monks, will not lead to confidence in those who are unconvinced, nor to increase in those who are convinced, but rather, monks, it will lead to lack of confidence in those who are unconvinced and to alteration in some of those who are convinced."

Atha kho bhagavā te [paṇḍukalohitake (syā.)] bhikkhū anekapariyāyena vigarahitvā dubbharatāya dupposatāya mahicchatāya asantuṭṭhitāya [asantuṭṭhatāya (syā.), asantuṭṭhiyā (sī.)] saṅgaṇikāya kosajjassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsitvā anekapariyāyena subharatāya suposatāya appicchassa santuṭṭhassa sallekhassa dhutassa pāsādikassa apacayassa vīriyārambhassa [viriyārambhassa (sī.), vīriyārabbhassa (ka.)] vaṇṇaṃ bhāsitvā bhikkhūnaṃ tadanucchavikaṃ tadanulomikaṃ dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ karotu. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ. Paṭhamaṃ paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū codetabbā, codetvā sāretabbā, sāretvā āpattiṃ [āpatti (sī. syā.)] āropetabbā, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Then the Blessed One, having rebuked those monks in many ways, criticizing them for being difficult to support, difficult to nourish, very ambitious, discontented, delighting in company, and lazy, spoke in many ways in praise of being easy to support, easy to nourish, having few desires, content, practicing austerity, practicing the ascetic practices, inspiring confidence, humility, and energetic effort. Having given the monks a Dhamma talk suitable and appropriate to the occasion, he addressed them: "Well then, monks, let the Saṅgha perform the act of censure on the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. And this, monks, is how it should be done. First, the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks should be admonished, then reminded, then made to incur an offense, and then a competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha:

3. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā kalahakārakā vivādakārakā bhassakārakā saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Esā ñatti.

3. "Venerable sir, may the Sangha listen to me. These pale-red monks are themselves makers of quarrels, makers of disputes, makers of conflicts, makers of arguments, makers of legal cases in the Sangha. And those other monks who are makers of quarrels, makers of disputes, makers of conflicts, makers of arguments, makers of legal cases in the Sangha, approach them and say: 'Do not, venerable ones, let this one win. Respond to him forcefully. You are wiser than him, more skilled than him, more learned than him, and more competent than him. Do not be afraid of him. We too will be on your side.' Because of this, quarrels that had not arisen now arise, and those that had arisen increase and grow. If the Sangha is ready, the Sangha should perform the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ karoti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable sir, may the Sangha hear me. These Paṇḍukalohitaka monks are themselves makers of quarrels... makers of legal cases in the Sangha. And they approach other monks who are makers of quarrels... makers of legal cases in the Sangha, and say to them: 'Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter strength with strength. You are wiser than him, more skilled than him, more learned than him, and more competent than him. Do not fear him. We too will be on your side.' As a result, quarrels that had not arisen now arise, and those that had arisen increase and grow. The Sangha performs the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. Let any venerable one who approves of performing the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks remain silent; let any who disapproves speak up."

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ karoti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the second time, I speak on this matter: Venerable sir, may the Sangha hear me. These Paṇḍukalohitaka monks are themselves makers of quarrels… makers of legal cases in the Sangha. And they approach other monks who are makers of quarrels… makers of legal cases in the Sangha, and say to them: ‘Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter strength with strength. You are wiser than him, more skilled than him, more learned than him, and more competent than him. Do not fear him. We too will be on your side.’ As a result, quarrels that had not arisen now arise, and those that had arisen increase and grow. The Sangha performs the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. Let any venerable one who approves of performing the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks remain silent; let any who disapproves speak up.

‘‘Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū attanā bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā, yepi caññe bhikkhū bhaṇḍanakārakā…pe… saṅghe adhikaraṇakārakā te upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘mā kho tumhe, āyasmanto, eso ajesi. Balavābalavaṃ paṭimantetha. Tumhe tena paṇḍitatarā ca byattatarā ca bahussutatarā ca alamattatarā ca. Mā cassa bhāyittha. Mayampi tumhākaṃ pakkhā bhavissāmā’ti. Tena anuppannāni ceva bhaṇḍanāni uppajjanti, uppannāni ca bhaṇḍanāni bhiyyobhāvāya vepullāya saṃvattanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ karoti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the third time, I speak on this matter: Venerable sir, may the Sangha hear me. These Paṇḍukalohitaka monks are themselves makers of quarrels… makers of legal cases in the Sangha. And they approach other monks who are makers of quarrels… makers of legal cases in the Sangha, and say to them: ‘Do not, venerable ones, let him win. Counter strength with strength. You are wiser than him, more skilled than him, more learned than him, and more competent than him. Do not fear him. We too will be on your side.’ As a result, quarrels that had not arisen now arise, and those that had arisen increase and grow. The Sangha performs the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. Let any venerable one who approves of performing the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks remain silent; let any who disapproves speak up.

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The Sangha has carried out the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. The Sangha approves; therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it to be.

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Group of Twelve Unrighteous Actions

4. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca [adhammakammañceva (syā.)] hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

4. Monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done in the absence (of the accused), done without questioning (him), done without admission (of the offense) — a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three other factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done for a non-offense, done for an offense not leading to confession, done for an offense that has been confessed—an act of censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three other factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without formally charging, done without scrutinizing, done without charging the offense—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three other factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done in the absence (of the accused), done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three other factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without inquiry, done unlawfully, done by a faction—an act of censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three other factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without acknowledgement, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done for a non-offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done for an offense not amenable to confession, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done for a confessed offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without accusation, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without inquiry, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a censure endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased. It is done without an offense being charged, done unlawfully, done by a faction—a censure endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and badly appeased."

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Group of Twelve Unrighteous Actions is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The twelvefold lawful act.

5. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

5. Monks, an act of censure is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased when endowed with three factors. It is done face to face, done by questioning, and done upon admission. Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done for an offense, done for an offense requiring confession, done for an offense that was not confessed—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done after censuring, done after reminding, done after charging with an offense—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done face to face, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done after questioning, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done upon acknowledgement, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done because of an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done for an offense leading to disclosure, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done for an undeclared offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three other factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done after accusation, done in accordance with the Dhamma, and done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three other factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done after reminding, done in accordance with the Dhamma, and done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of censure endowed with three other factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased. It is done after charging with an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, and done by a united Saṅgha—Indeed, monks, an act of censure endowed with these three factors is a lawful action, a disciplinary action, and well-appeased.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The twelve kinds of legitimate disciplinary actions are concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ: The Sextet on Wishing

6. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

6. "Monks, a monk endowed with three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure. He is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, and a maker of verbal disputes in the Saṅgha, an instigator of disputes; he is foolish, incompetent, full of offenses, and unrepentant; he lives in association with householders, in unseemly association with householders. Monks, a monk endowed with these three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

"Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure. He is deficient in higher morality; he is deficient in conduct due to misconduct; he is deficient in view due to wrong view. Monks, a monk endowed with these three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

"Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure. He speaks in disparagement of the Buddha, speaks in disparagement of the Dhamma, and speaks in disparagement of the Saṅgha. Monks, a monk endowed with these three qualities may be subjected by the Saṅgha, should it wish, to the act of censure."

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

"Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on three monks. One is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, and a maker of verbal disputes in the Saṅgha, an instigator of disputes; one is foolish, incompetent, full of offenses, and unrepentant; one lives in association with householders, in unseemly association with householders. Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on these three monks."

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

"Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on three further monks. One is deficient in higher morality; one is deficient in conduct due to misconduct; and one is deficient in view due to wrong view. Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on these three monks."

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, tajjanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

"Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on three further monks. One speaks in disparagement of the Buddha, speaks in disparagement of the Dhamma, and speaks in disparagement of the Saṅgha. Monks, the Saṅgha, should it wish, may impose the act of censure on these three monks."

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Ākaṅkhamānachakka is finished.

Aṭṭhārasavattaṃ

Eighteen observances

7. ‘‘Tajjanīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti [sammati (syā.)] sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena tajjanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi [na bhikkhū bhikkhūhi (syā.)] sampayojetabba’’nti.

7. A monk who has been subjected to the act of censure, monks, should behave properly. And what is proper conduct in this case? He should not give ordination; he should not give dependence; he should not have a novice attend on him; he should not accept appointment as an advisor of nuns; even when appointed, he should not advise nuns. He should not commit the offense for which the Sangha has imposed the act of censure, nor another similar offense, nor one worse than that. He should not criticize the act, nor those who performed it. The Uposatha should not be set aside for a regular monk, nor the Pavarana; no formal statement should be made; no charge should be initiated; no opportunity should be demanded; he should not accuse; he should not remind; he should not associate with other monks.

Tajjanīyakamme aṭṭhārasavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen observances concerning Tajjanīyakamma have been concluded.

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The eighteen instances where there is to be no remission.

8. Atha kho saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ akāsi. Te saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattanti, lomaṃ pātenti, netthāraṃ vattanti, bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘‘mayaṃ, āvuso, saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattāma, lomaṃ pātema, netthāraṃ vattāma, kathaṃ nu kho amhehi paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe…. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

8. Then the Sangha performed the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks. Those monks, having been censured by the Sangha, behaved properly, made themselves amenable, practised the way of extrication, and approached the monks, saying: "Friends, we have been censured by the Sangha and are behaving properly, making ourselves amenable, practising the way of extrication. How should we proceed?" The monks reported this matter to the Blessed One… "Well then, monks, let the Sangha rescind the act of censure against the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks."

Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

"Monks, the act of censure against a monk possessing five qualities should not be revoked. He ordains, he gives dependence, he has a novice wait upon him, he approves the appointment as an instructor of nuns, and even though appointed, he instructs nuns. Monks, the act of censure against a monk possessing these five qualities should not be revoked."

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena tajjanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Further, monks, the act of censure against a monk possessing five qualities should not be revoked. He commits the offense for which the Sangha had imposed the act of censure, or another similar to it, or one even worse; he criticizes the act, he criticizes those who performed it. Monks, the act of censure against a monk possessing these five qualities should not be revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti [bhikkhū bhikkhūhi sampayojeti (syā.)] – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, a monk endowed with eight qualities should not have the act of censure revoked. He prevents a normal monk from observing the Uposatha, he prevents the Pavāraṇā, he makes a matter for reproach, he establishes grounds for complaint, he requests an opportunity (to speak), he accuses, he reproaches, and he stirs up monks against one another. Indeed, monks, the act of censure against a monk possessing these eight qualities should not be revoked.

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen instances where there is to be no remission are completed.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The Eighteen Revocations.

9. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

9. Monks, for a monk endowed with five qualities, the act of censure should be rescinded. He does not give higher ordination, he does not give dependence, he does not supervise a novice, he does not accept the appointment to advise nuns, and even if appointed, he does not advise the nuns—Monks, for a monk endowed with these five qualities, the act of censure should be rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena tajjanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, Monks, for a monk endowed with five qualities, the act of censure should be revoked. He does not commit the offense for which the Saṅgha carried out the act of censure, nor another similar to it, nor one worse than that; he does not disparage the act, nor those who carried it out. Monks, for a monk endowed with these five qualities, the act of censure should be revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, for a monk endowed with eight qualities, the act of censure should be rescinded.

Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

He does not suspend the Uposatha of a monk in full standing; he does not suspend the Pavāraṇā; he does not issue a formal charge; he does not initiate an accusation; he does not cause a disturbance; he does not reprove; he does not admonish; he does not entangle monks—Monks, for a monk endowed with these eight qualities, the act of censure should be rescinded.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Eighteen Revocations are completed.

10. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tehi, bhikkhave, paṇḍukalohitakehi bhikkhūhi saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘mayaṃ, bhante, saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattāma, lomaṃ pātema, netthāraṃ vattāma, tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmā’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

10. And, monks, this is how it should be revoked. Those monks who have incurred the censure should approach the Saṅgha, arrange their upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior monks, sit in a squatting position, raise their joined palms, and say this: ‘Venerable sirs, we who have been subjected to the act of censure by the Saṅgha are behaving properly, we are amenable, we are conducting ourselves blamelessly, and we request the revocation of the act of censure.’ They should make this request a second time. They should make this request a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattanti, lomaṃ pātenti, netthāraṃ vattanti, tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācanti. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Let the Saṅgha hear me, venerable sirs. These monks, who were subjected to the act of censure by the Saṅgha, are conducting themselves properly, are amenable, are conducting themselves blamelessly, and request the revocation of the act of censure. If it is fitting for the Saṅgha, the Saṅgha should rescind the act of censure for these monks. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattanti, lomaṃ pātenti, netthāraṃ vattanti, tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Let the Saṅgha hear me, venerable sirs. These monks, who were subjected to the act of censure by the Saṅgha, are conducting themselves properly, are amenable, are conducting themselves blamelessly, and request the revocation of the act of censure. The Saṅgha rescinds the act of censure for these monks. If the revocation of the act of censure for these monks is agreeable to any venerable one, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattanti, lomaṃ pātenti, netthāraṃ vattanti, tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

A second time I declare this matter: Let the Saṅgha hear me, venerable sirs. These monks, who were subjected to the act of censure by the Saṅgha, are conducting themselves properly, are amenable, are conducting themselves blamelessly, and request the revocation of the act of censure. The Saṅgha rescinds the act of censure for these monks. If the revocation of the act of censure for these monks is agreeable to any venerable one, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime paṇḍukalohitakā bhikkhū saṅghena tajjanīyakammakatā sammā vattanti, lomaṃ pātenti, netthāraṃ vattanti, tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācanti. Saṅgho paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

A third time I declare this matter: Let the Saṅgha hear me, venerable sirs. These Paṇḍukalohitaka monks, who were subjected to the act of censure by the Saṅgha, are conducting themselves properly, are amenable, are conducting themselves blamelessly, and request the revocation of the act of censure. The Saṅgha rescinds the act of censure for these monks. If the revocation of the act of censure for these monks is agreeable to any venerable one, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena paṇḍukalohitakānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ tajjanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa,

The act of censure for the Paṇḍukalohitaka monks has been rescinded by the Saṅgha. It is agreeable to the Saṅgha.

Tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

Therefore, there is silence. Thus I hold it to be.

Tajjanīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ paṭhamaṃ.

The first censure act is completed.

### 2. Niyassakammaṃ - The act of dependence. ^2

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^2|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.2" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


3. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā seyyasako bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā [pakatattā (sī. syā.)] parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma āyasmā seyyasako bālo bhavissati abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharissati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

4. At that time, Venerable Seyyasaka was foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment. He lived in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them. Moreover, the monks regularly gave him probation, subjected him to reversion to the root, imposed penance, and reinstated him. Those monks who were modest… murmured, were displeased, and protested: "How can Venerable Seyyasaka be so foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment? How can he live in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them? And how can the monks regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him?" Then those monks reported the matter to the Blessed One.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, seyyasako bhikkhu bālo abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, bhikkhave, tassa moghapurisassa ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma so, bhikkhave, moghapuriso bālo bhavissati abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharissati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ [niyasakammaṃ (ka.)] karotu – nissāya te vatthabbanti. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ. Paṭhamaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu codetabbo, codetvā sāretabbo, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbo [āpatti āropetabbā (sī. syā.)], āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Then the Blessed One, regarding this incident and this matter, having convened the Sangha of monks, questioned the monks: "Is it true, monks, that the monk Seyyasaka is foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment; that he lives in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them; and that monks regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked him: "Monks, for that worthless man, this is unsuitable, unbecoming, inappropriate, not in accordance with the life of a recluse, impermissible, not to be done. How could that worthless man, monks, be foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment; live in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them; and for monks to regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him? This will not lead to confidence in those who lack it… Having rebuked him… he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Well then, monks, let the Sangha carry out the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka—he should live in dependence. And this is how it should be done. First, the monk Seyyasaka should be charged; having been charged, he should be reminded; having been reminded, he should be charged with the offense; having been charged with the offense, a monk who is competent and capable should inform the Sangha…"

12. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu bālo abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ kareyya – nissāya te vatthabbanti. Esā ñatti.

12. "Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Seyyasaka is foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment; he lives in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them; and monks regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him. If it seems fit to the Saṅgha, the Saṅgha should carry out the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka—he should live in dependence. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu bālo abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā. Saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ karoti – nissāya te vatthabbanti. Yassāyasmato khamati seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – nissāya te vatthabbanti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Seyyasaka is foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment; he lives in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them; and that monks regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him. The Saṅgha carries out the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka—he should live in dependence. If it is agreeable to the venerable ones that the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka be carried out—he should live in dependence—let them be silent. If it is not agreeable to anyone, let him speak."

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu bālo abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi; apissu bhikkhū pakatā parivāsaṃ dentā mūlāya paṭikassantā mānattaṃ dentā abbhentā. Saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ karoti – nissāya te vatthabbanti. Yassāyasmato khamati seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – nissāya te vatthabbanti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the second time I speak on this matter [...]; for the third time I speak on this matter—Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Seyyasaka is foolish, inept, prone to offenses, and not giving rise to their abandonment; he lives in close association with householders, engaging in unsuitable interactions with them; and monks regularly give him probation, subject him to reversion to the root, impose penance, and reinstate him. The Saṅgha carries out the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka—he should live in dependence. If it is agreeable to the venerable ones that the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka be carried out—he should live in dependence—let him be silent. If it is not agreeable to anyone, let him speak.

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ – nissāya te vatthabbanti. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The Saṅgha has carried out the act of dependence for the monk Seyyasaka—he should live in dependence. It is agreeable to the Saṅgha, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Group of Twelve Unrighteous Actions

13. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

13. Monks, an act of suspension endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle. It is done in the absence (of the accused), done without questioning, done without acknowledgment—endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

Further, monks, an act of suspension endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle. It is done for a non-offense, done for an offense not entailing confession, done for an offense already confessed—endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

Further, monks, an act of suspension endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle. It is done without accusation, done without examination, done without charging the offense—endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Further, monks... done in the absence (of the accused), done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Further, monks... done without questioning, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Further, monks... done without acknowledgment, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, monks, an act of suspension endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle. It is done for a non-offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and hard to settle.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, monks... done for an offense not entailing confession, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Further, monks... done for a confessed offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, monks...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done without being charged, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done without being reminded, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a dependent act endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and poorly settled. It is done without charging with an offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, bhikkhus, a dependent act is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and poorly settled.

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on Twelve Unlawful Acts is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Section on Twelve Lawful Acts.

14. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

14.Bhikkhus, a dependent act endowed with three factors is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled. It is done in the presence, done upon questioning, and done upon acknowledgment—endowed with these three factors, bhikkhus, a dependent act is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a dependent act endowed with three factors is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled. It is done concerning an offense, done concerning an offense requiring declaration, done concerning an undeclared offense—endowed with these three factors, bhikkhus, a dependent act is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a dependent act endowed with three factors is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled. It is done after accusing, done after reminding, done after charging with an offense—endowed with these three factors, bhikkhus, a dependent act is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done in the presence, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done upon questioning, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done upon acknowledgment, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done concerning an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done concerning an offense requiring declaration, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done concerning an undeclared offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done after accusing, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave…pe….

Furthermore, bhikkhus, ...it is done after reminding, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these factors, bhikkhus, ...

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ niyassakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a dependent act endowed with three factors is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled. It is done after charging with an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Saṅgha—endowed with these three factors, bhikkhus, a dependent act is both a lawful act and a disciplinary act, and it is well-settled.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on Twelve Lawful Acts is concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ

The Six Things Wished For.

15. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

15.Bhikkhus, a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition. What three? Here, a bhikkhu is quarrelsome, a creator of disputes, a debater, a babbler, one who causes legal issues in the Saṅgha; he is foolish, incompetent, prone to offenses, and unyielding; he lives in association with householders in inappropriate ways. It is with these three qualities, bhikkhus, that a bhikkhu may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition. What three? Here, a bhikkhu is deficient in higher virtue, deficient in conduct, and deficient in higher view. It is with these three qualities, bhikkhus, that a bhikkhu may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition. What three? Here, a bhikkhu speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, and speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. It is with these three qualities, bhikkhus, that a bhikkhu may, if the Saṅgha wishes, be subjected to an act of imposition.

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti, abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

Bhikkhus, the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition on three bhikkhus. What three? Here, one is quarrelsome, a creator of disputes, a debater, a babbler, one who causes legal issues in the Saṅgha; one is foolish, incompetent, prone to offenses, and unyielding; one lives in association with householders in inappropriate ways. It is on these three bhikkhus, bhikkhus, that the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition on three other bhikkhus. What three? Here, one is deficient in higher virtue, one is deficient in conduct, and one is deficient in higher view. It is on these three bhikkhus, bhikkhus, that the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, niyassakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, bhikkhus, the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition on three other bhikkhus. What three? Here, one speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, one speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, and one speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. It is on these three bhikkhus, bhikkhus, that the Saṅgha may, if it wishes, impose an act of imposition.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on What Is Wished For is concluded.

Aṭṭhārasavattaṃ

Eighteen Observances

16. ‘‘Niyassakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena niyassakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kārāpetabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

16.Bhikkhus, a bhikkhu on whom the act of dependence has been performed should conduct himself properly. Herein is the proper conduct: he should not give ordination; he should not grant dependence; he should not have a novice attend him; the appointment of him as instructor of nuns should not be accepted; and nuns should not be advised, even if authorized. He should not commit the offense for which the Sangha performed the act of dependence, nor any similar offense, nor one even more serious than that; the deed should not be criticized, nor the doers of the deed. The Uposatha of a bhikkhu in good standing should not be suspended, nor should the Pavāraṇā be suspended; he should not be made to give a statement; an accusation should not be preferred; no occasion should be given; he should not be questioned; he should not be prompted; and he should not be associated with bhikkhus.

Niyassakamme aṭṭhārasavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Eighteen Observances concerning the Act of Dependence are concluded.

17. Atha kho saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ akāsi – nissāya te vatthabbanti. So saṅghena niyassakammakato kalyāṇamitte sevamāno bhajamāno payirupāsamāno uddisāpento paripucchanto bahussuto hoti, āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. Sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘ahaṃ, āvuso, saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe…. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

17.Then the Sangha performed the act of dependence on the bhikkhu Seyyasaka, saying: 'You must dwell in dependence.' Having been subjected to the act of dependence by the Sangha, associating with good friends, keeping company with them, and attending upon them, asking for instruction and questioning, he became learned, a master of tradition, a bearer of the Dhamma, a bearer of the Vinaya, a bearer of the matrices, wise, competent, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He conducted himself properly, made progress, and penetrated the teaching. Approaching the bhikkhus, he said: 'Friends, I have been subjected to the act of dependence by the Sangha. I conduct myself properly, make progress, and penetrate the teaching. How should I proceed?' The bhikkhus reported this matter to the Blessed One… 'Well then, bhikkhus, let the Sangha revoke the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka.'

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The Eighteen Cases Where It Should Not Be Revoked.

18. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

18.Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, the act of dependence should not be revoked. He gives ordination, he grants dependence, he has a novice attend on him, he accepts appointment as an instructor of nuns, and when appointed, he instructs nuns—these, monks, are the five factors for which the act of dependence should not be revoked.

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena niyassakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Further, monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, the act of dependence should not be revoked. He commits the offense for which the Saṅgha imposed the act of dependence, or another similar to it, or one even worse; he disparages the act, he disparages those who carried out the act—these, monks, are the five factors for which the act of dependence should not be revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with eight factors, the act of dependence should not be revoked. He arranges the Uposatha for a normal bhikkhu, he arranges the Pavāraṇā, he makes himself available for admonition, he establishes proceedings against offenders, he seeks an opportunity (to speak), he rebukes, he reminds, and he properly involves bhikkhus—these, monks, are the eight factors for which the act of dependence should not be revoked.

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Eighteen Cases Where It Should Not Be Revoked are concluded.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The Eighteen Cases Where It Should Be Revoked.

19. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

19.Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, the act of dependence should be revoked. He does not give ordination, he does not grant dependence, he does not have a novice attend on him, he does not accept appointment as an instructor of nuns, and when appointed, he does not instruct nuns—monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, the act of dependence should be revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena niyassakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Further, monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, the act of dependence should be revoked. He does not commit the offense for which the Saṅgha imposed the act of dependence, or another similar to it, or one worse than that; he does not disparage the act, nor those who carried out the act. Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, the act of dependence should be revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with eight factors, the act of dependence should be revoked.

Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

He does not arrange the Uposatha for a normal bhikkhu, he does not arrange the Pavāraṇā, he does not make himself available for admonition, he does not establish proceedings against offenders, he does not seek an opportunity (to speak), he does not rebuke, he does not remind, and he does not properly involve bhikkhus—these, monks, are the eight factors for which the act of dependence should be revoked.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Eighteen Cases Where It Should Be Revoked are concluded.

20. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena, bhikkhave, seyyasakena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

20.And, monks, this is how it should be revoked. The bhikkhu who has been placed on probation should approach the Saṅgha, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior bhikkhus, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined palms, and say this: 'Venerable sirs, I, having been placed on probation by the Saṅgha, am conducting myself properly, am shaving my hair, am acting fittingly, and I request the revocation of the probation.' He should make this request a second time. He should make this request a third time. A competent and capable bhikkhu should then inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This bhikkhu Seyyasaka, who has been subjected to the act of dependence by the Saṅgha, is conducting himself properly, has shaved his hair, is acting fittingly, and requests the revocation of the act of dependence. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, may the Saṅgha revoke the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This bhikkhu Seyyasaka, who has been subjected to the act of dependence by the Saṅgha, is conducting himself properly, has shaved his hair, is acting fittingly, and requests the revocation of the act of dependence. The Saṅgha revokes the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka. Let those venerable ones who approve of the revocation of the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka remain silent; let those who do not approve speak.
