‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For a second time, I speak on this matter—Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This bhikkhu Seyyasaka, who has been subjected to the act of dependence by the Saṅgha, is conducting himself properly, has shaved his hair, is acting fittingly, and requests the revocation of the act of dependence. The Saṅgha revokes the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka. Let those venerable ones who approve of the revocation of the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka remain silent; let those who do not approve speak.

‘‘Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ seyyasako bhikkhu saṅghena niyassakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For a third time, I speak on this matter—Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This bhikkhu Seyyasaka, who has been subjected to the act of dependence by the Saṅgha, is conducting himself properly, has shaved his hair, is acting fittingly, and requests the revocation of the act of dependence. The Saṅgha revokes the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka. Let those venerable ones who approve of the revocation of the act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka remain silent; let those who do not approve speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena seyyasakassa bhikkhuno niyassakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The act of dependence for the bhikkhu Seyyasaka has been revoked by the Saṅgha. The Saṅgha assents, therefore it is silent; thus I hold it.

Niyassakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ dutiyaṃ.

The second act of dependence is concluded.

### 3. Pabbājanīyakammaṃ - The Act of Banishment. ^3

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^3|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.3" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


21. [idaṃ vatthu pārā. 431 ādayo] Tena kho pana samayena assajipunabbasukā nāma [nāma bhikkhū (ka.)] kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāsikā honti alajjino pāpabhikkhū. Te [cūḷava. 292 ādayo] evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācaranti – mālāvacchaṃ ropentipi ropāpentipi, siñcantipi siñcāpentipi, ocinantipi ocināpentipi, ganthentipi ganthāpentipi, ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, mañjarikaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, vidhūtikaṃ [vidhutikaṃ (syā.)] karontipi kārāpentipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, āveḷaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, uracchadaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi. Te kulitthīnaṃ kuladhītānaṃ kulakumārīnaṃ kulasuṇhānaṃ kuladāsīnaṃ ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, mañjarikaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, vidhūtikaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, āveḷaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, uracchadaṃ harantipi harāpentipi. Te kulitthīhi kuladhītāhi kulakumārīhi kulasuṇhāhi kuladāsīhi saddhiṃ ekabhājanepi bhuñjanti, ekathālakepi pivanti, ekāsanepi nisīdanti, ekamañcepi tuvaṭṭenti, ekattharaṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, ekapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, ekattharaṇapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, vikālepi bhuñjanti, majjampi pivanti, mālāgandhavilepanampi dhārenti, naccantipi, gāyantipi, vādentipi, lāsentipi; naccantiyāpi naccanti, naccantiyāpi gāyanti, naccantiyāpi vādenti, naccantiyāpi lāsenti; gāyantiyāpi naccanti, gāyantiyāpi gāyanti, gāyantiyāpi vādenti, gāyantiyāpi lāsenti; vādentiyāpi naccanti, vādentiyāpi gāyanti, vādentiyāpi vādenti, vādentiyāpi lāsenti; lāsentiyāpi naccanti, lāsentiyāpi gāyanti, lāsentiyāpi vādenti, lāsentiyāpi lāsenti; aṭṭhapadepi kīḷanti, dasapadepi kīḷanti, ākāsepi kīḷanti, parihārapathepi kīḷanti, santikāyapi kīḷanti, khalikāyapi kīḷanti, ghaṭikāyapi kīḷanti, salākahatthenapi kīḷanti, akkhenapi kīḷanti, paṅgacīrenapi kīḷanti, vaṅkakenapi kīḷanti, mokkhacikāyapi kīḷanti, ciṅgulakenapi kīḷanti, pattāḷhakenapi kīḷanti, rathakenapi kīḷanti, dhanukenapi kīḷanti, akkharikāyapi kīḷanti, manesikāyapi kīḷanti, yathāvajjenapi kīḷanti; hatthismimpi sikkhanti, assasmimpi sikkhanti, rathasmimpi sikkhanti, dhanusmimpi sikkhanti, tharusmimpi sikkhanti; hatthissapi purato dhāvanti, assassapi purato dhāvanti, rathassapi purato [purato dhāvanti (syā.)] dhāvantipi ādhāvantipi; usseḷentipi, apphoṭentipi, nibbujjhantipi, muṭṭhīhipi yujjhanti; raṅgamajjhepi saṅghāṭiṃ pattharitvā naccakiṃ [naccantiṃ (sī. syā.)] evaṃ vadanti – ‘‘idha, bhagini, naccassū’’ti; nalāṭikampi denti; vividhampi anācāraṃ ācaranti.

21.Now at that time, the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu were residing at Kīṭāgiri—shameless, wicked bhikkhus. They engaged in such improper conduct as follows: they cultivated flower plants themselves or had them cultivated, watered them themselves or had them watered, picked flowers themselves or had them picked, strung garlands themselves or had them strung, made single-stemmed garlands themselves or had them made, made double-stemmed garlands themselves or had them made, made nosegays themselves or had them made, made decorative bunches themselves or had them made, made chaplets themselves or had them made, made head-wreaths themselves or had them made, made chest-ornaments themselves or had them made. They carried single-stemmed garlands for women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female slaves of good families, or had them carried; and double-stemmed garlands, nosegays, decorative bunches, chaplets, head-wreaths, and chest-ornaments likewise. They ate from the same dish with women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female slaves of good families; they drank from the same bowl; they sat on the same seat; they lay on the same couch, on the same spread, on the same blanket, or on the same spread and blanket together. They ate at the wrong time, drank strong drink, wore garlands, perfumes, and unguents. They danced, sang, played music, and performed entertainments. They danced when others danced, sang when others sang, played music when others played, and performed entertainments when others performed entertainments. They danced when others sang, sang when others danced, played music when others danced, performed entertainments when others danced. They danced when others played music, sang when others played music, played music when others sang, performed entertainments when others sang. They danced when others performed entertainments, sang when others performed entertainments, played music when others performed entertainments, and performed entertainments when others played music. They played games such as eight-square chess, ten-square chess, playing at imaginary boards, playing at removing figures, playing at dice, playing at stick games, playing at games with painted sticks, playing at dice, playing at blowing through toy pipes, playing at toy plows, playing at turning somersaults, playing at toy windmills, playing at toy measures, playing at toy carts, playing at toy bows, playing at guessing letters, playing at guessing thoughts, and playing at mimicking deformities. They trained in elephant riding, horse riding, chariot driving, archery, and swordsmanship. They ran in front of elephants, ran in front of horses, ran in front of chariots, and raced alongside them. They shouted, clapped their hands, wrestled, and boxed. They spread their outer robes in the middle of an arena and said to a dancing girl, “Dance here, sister!” They gave her a forehead-gift. They engaged in various kinds of improper conduct.

22. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu kāsīsu vassaṃvuṭṭho [vassaṃvuttho (sī. syā.)] sāvatthiṃ gacchanto bhagavantaṃ dassanāya yena kīṭāgiri tadavasari. Atha kho so bhikkhu pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya kīṭāgiriṃ piṇḍāya pāvisi pāsādikena abhikkantena paṭikkantena ālokitena vilokitena samiñjitena [sammiñjitena (sī. syā. kaṃ.)] pasāritena, okkhittacakkhu iriyāpathasampanno. Manussā taṃ bhikkhuṃ passitvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘kvāyaṃ abalabalo viya mandamando viya bhākuṭikabhākuṭiko viya? Ko imassa upagatassa piṇḍakampi dassati? Amhākaṃ pana ayyā assajipunabbasukā saṇhā sakhilā sukhasambhāsā mihitapubbaṅgamā ehisvāgatavādino abbhākuṭikā uttānamukhā pubbabhāsino. Tesaṃ kho nāma piṇḍo dātabbo’’ti.

22.Now at that time, a certain bhikkhu who had spent the rains in Kāsī, while traveling to Sāvatthī to see the Blessed One, arrived at Kīṭāgiri. Then that bhikkhu, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and entered Kīṭāgiri for alms. He was dignified in his going forth and returning, in looking and glancing, in bending and stretching, with downcast eyes and perfect deportment. When the people saw that bhikkhu, they said: “Who is this, feeble as if weak, sluggish as if dull, frowning as if scowling? Who will give alms to one who has approached like this? But our venerable ones, Assaji and Punabbasu, are gentle, amiable, pleasant to converse with, with smiles preceding them, saying ‘Come! Welcome!’, cheerful, with open faces, and speaking first. Indeed, it is to them that alms should be given.”

Addasā kho aññataro upāsako taṃ bhikkhuṃ kīṭāgirismiṃ piṇḍāya carantaṃ; disvāna yena so bhikkhu tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā taṃ bhikkhuṃ abhivādetvā etadavoca – ‘‘api, bhante, piṇḍo labbhatī’’ti? ‘‘Na kho, āvuso, piṇḍo labbhatī’’ti. ‘‘Ehi, bhante, gharaṃ gamissāmā’’ti. Atha kho so upāsako taṃ bhikkhuṃ gharaṃ netvā bhojetvā etadavoca – ‘‘kahaṃ, bhante, ayyo gamissatī’’ti? ‘‘Sāvatthiṃ kho ahaṃ, āvuso, gamissāmi bhagavantaṃ dassanāyā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, bhante, mama vacanena bhagavato pāde sirasā vanda, evañca vadehi – ‘duṭṭho, bhante, kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāso. Assajipunabbasukā nāma kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāsikā alajjino pāpabhikkhū. Te evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācaranti – mālāvacchaṃ ropentipi ropāpentipi, siñcantipi siñcāpentipi, ocinantipi, ocināpentipi, ganthentipi ganthāpentipi, ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, mañjarikaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, vidhūtikaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, āveḷaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi, uracchadaṃ karontipi kārāpentipi. Te kulitthīnaṃ kuladhītānaṃ kulakumārīnaṃ kulasuṇhānaṃ kuladāsīnaṃ ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, mañjarikaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, vidhūtikaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, āveḷaṃ harantipi harāpentipi, uracchadaṃ harantipi harāpentipi. Te kulitthīhi kuladhītāhi kulakumārīhi kulasuṇhāhi kuladāsīhi saddhiṃ ekabhājanepi bhuñjanti, ekathālakepi pivanti, ekāsanepi nisīdanti, ekamañcepi tuvaṭṭenti, ekattharaṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, ekapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, ekattharaṇapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭenti, vikālepi bhuñjanti, majjampi pivanti, mālāgandhavilepanampi dhārenti, naccantipi, gāyantipi, vādentipi, lāsentipi; naccantiyāpi naccanti, naccantiyāpi gāyanti, naccantiyāpi vādenti, naccantiyāpi lāsenti…pe… (cakkaṃ kātabbaṃ). Lāsentiyāpi naccanti, lāsentiyāpi gāyanti, lāsentiyāpi vādenti, lāsentiyāpi lāsenti; aṭṭhapadepi kīḷanti, dasapadepi kīḷanti, ākāsepi kīḷanti, parihārapathepi kīḷanti, santikāyapi kīḷanti, khalikāyapi kīḷanti, ghaṭikāyapi kīḷanti, salākahatthenapi kīḷanti, akkhenapi kīḷanti, paṅgacīrenapi kīḷanti, vaṅkakenapi kīḷanti, mokkhacikāyapi kīḷanti, ciṅgulakenapi kīḷanti, pattāḷhakenapi kīḷanti, rathakenapi kīḷanti, dhanukenapi kīḷanti, akkharikāyapi kīḷanti, manesikāyapi kīḷanti, yathāvajjenapi kīḷanti; hatthismimpi sikkhanti, assasmimpi sikkhanti, rathasmimpi sikkhanti, dhanusmimpi sikkhanti, tharusmimpi sikkhanti; hatthissapi purato dhāvanti, assassapi purato dhāvanti, rathassapi purato dhāvantipi ādhāvantipi; usseḷentipi, apphoṭentipi, nibbujjhantipi, muṭṭhīhipi yujjhanti; raṅgamajjhepi saṅghāṭiṃ pattharitvā naccakiṃ evaṃ vadanti – ‘idha, bhagini, naccassū’ti; nalāṭikampi denti; vividhampi anācāraṃ ācaranti. Yepi te, bhante, manussā pubbe saddhā ahesuṃ pasannā tepi etarahi assaddhā appasannā. Yānipi tāni saṅghassa pubbe dānapathāni tānipi etarahi upacchinnāni. Riñcanti pesalā bhikkhū, nivasanti pāpabhikkhū. Sādhu, bhante, bhagavā kīṭāgiriṃ bhikkhū pahiṇeyya, yathāyaṃ kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāso saṇṭhaheyyā’’ti.

Then a certain lay follower saw that bhikkhu going for alms in Kīṭāgiri. Having seen him, he approached that bhikkhu, paid homage to him, and said: “Venerable sir, have you received almsfood?” “No, friend, I have not received almsfood.” “Come, venerable sir, let us go to my home.” Then that lay follower took that bhikkhu to his home, fed him, and said: “Where are you going, venerable sir?” “I am going to Sāvatthī, friend, to see the Blessed One.” “Then, venerable sir, in my name, bow your head at the feet of the Blessed One and say: ‘Venerable sir, the dwelling at Kīṭāgiri is corrupted. The bhikkhus named Assaji and Punabbasu, residents of Kīṭāgiri, are shameless, wicked bhikkhus. They engage in such improper conduct as follows: they cultivated flower plants themselves or had them cultivated, watered them themselves or had them watered, picked flowers themselves or had them picked, strung garlands themselves or had them strung, made single-stemmed garlands themselves or had them made, made double-stemmed garlands themselves or had them made, made nosegays themselves or had them made, made decorative bunches themselves or had them made, made chaplets themselves or had them made, made head-wreaths themselves or had them made, made chest-ornaments themselves or had them made. They carried single-stemmed garlands for women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female slaves of good families, or had them carried; and double-stemmed garlands, nosegays, decorative bunches, chaplets, head-wreaths, and chest-ornaments likewise. They ate from the same dish with women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female slaves of good families; they drank from the same bowl; they sat on the same seat; they lay on the same couch, on the same spread, on the same blanket, or on the same spread and blanket together. They ate at the wrong time, drank strong drink, wore garlands, perfumes, and unguents. They danced, sang, played music, and performed entertainments. They danced when others danced, sang when others sang, played music when others played, and performed entertainments when others performed entertainments. They danced when others sang, sang when others danced, played music when others danced, performed entertainments when others danced. They danced when others played music, sang when others played music, played music when others sang, performed entertainments when others sang. They danced when others performed entertainments, sang when others performed entertainments, played music when others performed entertainments, and performed entertainments when others played music. They played games such as eight-square chess, ten-square chess, playing at imaginary boards, playing at removing figures, playing at dice, playing at stick games, playing at games with painted sticks, playing at dice, playing at blowing through toy pipes, playing at toy plows, playing at turning somersaults, playing at toy windmills, playing at toy measures, playing at toy carts, playing at toy bows, playing at guessing letters, playing at guessing thoughts, and playing at mimicking deformities. They trained in elephant riding, horse riding, chariot driving, archery, and swordsmanship. They ran in front of elephants, ran in front of horses, ran in front of chariots, and raced alongside them. They shouted, clapped their hands, wrestled, and boxed. They spread their outer robes in the middle of an arena and said to a dancing girl, “Dance here, sister!” They gave her a forehead-gift. They engaged in various kinds of improper conduct. Those people, venerable sir, who were formerly faithful and devoted have now become faithless and un-devoted. Those former alms routes for the Saṅgha have now been cut off. The virtuous bhikkhus leave, while the wicked bhikkhus stay. It would be good, venerable sir, if the Blessed One would send bhikkhus to Kīṭāgiri so that this dwelling at Kīṭāgiri might be restored.’”

‘‘Evamāvuso’’ti kho so bhikkhu tassa upāsakassa paṭissuṇitvā uṭṭhāyāsanā yena sāvatthi tena pakkāmi. Anupubbena yena sāvatthi jetavanaṃ anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāmo yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Āciṇṇaṃ kho panetaṃ buddhānaṃ bhagavantānaṃ āgantukehi bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ paṭisammodituṃ. Atha kho bhagavā taṃ bhikkhuṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kacci, bhikkhu, khamanīyaṃ, kacci yāpanīyaṃ, kaccisi appakilamathena addhānaṃ āgato, kuto ca tvaṃ bhikkhu āgacchasī’’ti? ‘‘Khamanīyaṃ, bhagavā, yāpanīyaṃ bhagavā; appakilamathena ca ahaṃ, bhante, addhānaṃ āgato. Idhāhaṃ, bhante, kāsīsu vassaṃvuṭṭho sāvatthiṃ āgacchanto bhagavantaṃ dassanāya yena kīṭāgiri tadavasariṃ. Atha khvāhaṃ, bhante, pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya kīṭāgiriṃ piṇḍāya pāvisiṃ. Addasā kho maṃ, bhante, aññataro upāsako kīṭāgirismiṃ piṇḍāya carantaṃ; disvāna yenāhaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā maṃ abhivādetvā etadavoca – ‘api, bhante, piṇḍo labbhatī’ti. ‘Na kho, āvuso, piṇḍo labbhatī’ti. ‘Ehi, bhante, gharaṃ gamissāmā’ti. Atha kho, bhante, so upāsako maṃ gharaṃ netvā bhojetvā etadavoca – ‘kahaṃ, bhante, ayyo gamissatī’ti? ‘Sāvatthiṃ kho ahaṃ, āvuso, gamissāmi bhagavantaṃ dassanāyā’ti. ‘Tena hi, bhante, mama vacanena bhagavato pāde sirasā vanda, evañca vadehi – duṭṭho, bhante, kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāso. Assajipunabbasukā nāma kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāsikā alajjino pāpabhikkhū. Te evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācaranti – mālāvacchaṃ ropentipi ropāpentipi…pe… vividhampi anācāraṃ ācaranti. Yepi te, bhante, manussā pubbe saddhā ahesuṃ pasannā tepi etarahi assaddhā appasannā. Yānipi tāni saṅghassa pubbe dānapathāni tānipi etarahi upacchinnāni. Riñcanti pesalā bhikkhū, nivasanti pāpabhikkhū. Sādhu, bhante, bhagavā kīṭāgiriṃ bhikkhū pahiṇeyya, yathāyaṃ kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāso saṇṭhaheyyā’ti. Tato ahaṃ bhagavā āgacchāmī’’ti.

“Very well, friend,” the monk replied, and rising from his seat, he set out for Sāvatthī. Traveling stage by stage, he arrived at Sāvatthī, Jeta’s Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika’s monastery, and approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Now it is the Blessed One’s custom to exchange greetings with monks who have arrived. Then the Blessed One said to him: “I hope, monk, you are keeping well, I hope you are comfortable, and I hope you have come without much fatigue. From where have you come, monk?” “I am keeping well, Blessed One; I am comfortable, Blessed One. And I have come without much fatigue, venerable sir. Here, venerable sir, having spent the rains in Kāsi, I was on my way to Sāvatthī to see the Blessed One when I turned aside to Kīṭāgiri. Then, venerable sir, in the morning, having dressed and taken my bowl and robe, I entered Kīṭāgiri for alms. A certain lay follower saw me wandering for alms in Kīṭāgiri. Having seen me, he approached, paid homage to me, and said: ‘Venerable sir, have you obtained alms?’ ‘No, friend, I have not obtained alms.’ ‘Come, venerable sir, let us go to my house.’ Then, venerable sir, that lay follower took me to his house, fed me, and said: ‘Where, venerable sir, are you going?’ ‘I am going to Sāvatthī, friend, to see the Blessed One.’ ‘Then, venerable sir, bow your head at the Blessed One’s feet in my name and say this: “Venerable sir, the dwelling at Kīṭāgiri is corrupt. The monks named Assaji and Punabbasuka residing at Kīṭāgiri are shameless, wicked monks. They engage in such improper conduct: they plant and have others plant flower gardens…they engage in various kinds of improper conduct. Those people, venerable sir, who were formerly faithful and devoted have now become faithless and undevoted. Those former avenues of alms for the Saṅgha have now been cut off. Virtuous monks are leaving, and wicked monks are staying. It would be good, venerable sir, if the Blessed One would send monks to Kīṭāgiri so that the dwelling there might be restored.”’ Then, Blessed One, I have come to you.”

23. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, assajipunabbasukā nāma kīṭāgirismiṃ āvāsikā alajjino pāpabhikkhū? Te evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācaranti – mālāvacchaṃ ropentipi…pe… vividhampi anācāraṃ ācaranti? Yepi te manussā pubbe saddhā ahesuṃ pasannā tepi etarahi assaddhā appasannā? Yānipi tāni saṅghassa pubbe dānapathāni tānipi etarahi upacchinnāni? Riñcanti pesalā bhikkhū nivasanti pāpabhikkhū’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ…pe… kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācarissanti – mālāvacchaṃ ropessantipi ropāpessantipi, siñcissantipi siñcāpessantipi, ocinissantipi ocināpessantipi, ganthessantipi ganthāpessantipi, ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, mañjarikaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, vidhūtikaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, āveḷaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi, uracchadaṃ karissantipi kārāpessantipi. Te kulitthīnaṃ kuladhītānaṃ kulakumārīnaṃ kulasuṇhānaṃ kuladāsīnaṃ ekatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, ubhatovaṇṭikamālaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, mañjarikaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, vidhūtikaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, vaṭaṃsakaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, āveḷaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi, uracchadaṃ harissantipi harāpessantipi. Te kulitthīhi kuladhītāhi kulakumārīhi kulasuṇhāhi kuladāsīhi saddhiṃ ekabhājanepi bhuñjissanti, ekathālakepi pivissanti, ekāsanepi nisīdissanti, ekamañcepi tuvaṭṭissanti, ekattharaṇāpi tuvaṭṭissanti, ekapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭissanti, ekattharaṇapāvuraṇāpi tuvaṭṭissanti, vikālepi bhuñjissanti, majjampi pivissanti, mālāgandhavilepanampi dhāressanti, naccissantipi, gāyissantipi, vādessantipi, lāsessantipi; naccantiyāpi naccissanti, naccantiyāpi gāyissanti, naccantiyāpi vādessanti, naccantiyāpi lāsessanti; gāyantiyāpi naccissanti, gāyantiyāpi gāyissanti, gāyantiyāpi vādessanti, gāyantiyāpi lāsessanti; vādentiyāpi naccissanti, vādentiyāpi gāyissanti, vādentiyāpi vādessanti, vādentiyāpi lāsessanti; lāsentiyāpi naccissanti, lāsentiyāpi gāyissanti, lāsentiyāpi vādessanti; lāsentiyāpi lāsessanti; aṭṭhapadepi kīḷissanti, dasapadepi kīḷissanti, ākāsepi kīḷissanti, parihārapathepi kīḷissanti, santikāyapi kīḷissanti, khalikāyapi kīḷissanti, ghaṭikāyapi kīḷissanti, salākahatthenapi kīḷissanti, akkhenapi kīḷissanti, paṅgacīrenapi kīḷissanti, vaṅkakenapi kīḷissanti mokkhacikāyapi kīḷissanti, ciṅgulakenapi kīḷissanti, pattāḷhakenapi kīḷissanti, rathakenapi kīḷissanti, dhanukenapi kīḷissanti, akkharikāyapi kīḷissanti, manesikāyapi kīḷissanti, yathāvajjenapi kīḷissanti; hatthismimpi sikkhissanti, assasmimpi sikkhissanti, rathasmimpi sikkhissanti, dhanusmimpi sikkhissanti, tharusmimpi sikkhissanti; hatthissapi purato dhāvissanti, assassapi purato dhāvissanti, rathassapi purato [purato dhāvissanti (syā.)] dhāvissantipi ādhāvissantipi; usseḷessantipi, apphoṭessantipi, nibbujjhissantipi, muṭṭhīhipi yujjhissanti; raṅgamajjhepi saṅghāṭiṃ pattharitvā naccakiṃ evaṃ vakkhanti [vadissanti (ka.)] – ‘idha, bhagini, naccassū’ti; nalāṭikampi dassanti; vividhampi anācāraṃ ācarissanti. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā sāriputtamoggallāne āmantesi – ‘‘gacchatha tumhe, sāriputtā, kīṭāgiriṃ gantvā assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ karotha, tumhākaṃ ete saddhivihārino’’ti.

23.Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and in connection with this matter, had the Bhikkhu Saṅgha assembled and questioned the bhikkhus: “Is it true, bhikkhus, that the bhikkhus named Assaji and Punabbasu, residing at Kīṭāgiri, are shameless, evil bhikkhus? That they engage in such improper conduct—planting garland-creepers, and so on, and engaging in various other improper kinds of conduct? And that those people who were formerly faithful and devoted have now become faithless and undevoted? And that the former avenues of offerings to the Saṅgha have now been cut off? And that virtuous bhikkhus are disregarded, while evil bhikkhus reside there?” “It is true, Bhante,” they replied. The Blessed One, the Buddha, rebuked them: “It is unsuitable… How, bhikkhus, can these foolish men engage in such improper conduct? They plant garland-creepers and have them planted; they water them and have them watered; they pluck flowers and have them plucked; they string garlands and have them strung; they make single-stem garlands and have them made; they make double-stem garlands and have them made; they make bunches of flowers and have them made; they make whisks and have them made; they make pendants and have them made; they make wreaths and have them made; they make breast ornaments and have them made. They carry single-stem garlands, double-stem garlands, bunches of flowers, whisks, pendants, wreaths, and breast ornaments to women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female servants of good families, and have them carried. They eat from the same dish with women of good families, daughters of good families, maidens of good families, daughters-in-law of good families, and female servants of good families; they drink from the same bowl; they sit on the same seat; they lie on the same couch; they lie on the same mattress; they lie on the same coverlet; they lie on the same mattress and coverlet. They eat at unseasonable times; they drink alcohol; they wear garlands, perfumes, and cosmetics. They dance, sing, play musical instruments, and perform theatrical dances. They dance when others are dancing, sing when others are singing, play musical instruments when others are playing, perform theatrical dances when others are performing theatrical dances. They dance when others are singing, sing when others are singing, play musical instruments when others are singing, perform theatrical dances when others are singing. They dance when others are playing music, sing when others are playing music, play musical instruments when others are playing music, perform theatrical dances when others are playing music. They dance when others are performing theatrical dances, sing when others are performing theatrical dances, play musical instruments when others are performing theatrical dances, perform theatrical dances when others are performing theatrical dances. They play eight-square games, ten-square games, games in the air, games on a course, games of chance, games with sticks, games with dice, games with sticks in hand, games with dice, games with bent reeds, release games, games with swings, games with leaf-baskets, games with toy chariots, games with toy bows, letter games, mind-guessing games, and games of mimicry. They train in elephant riding, horse riding, chariot driving, archery, and swordsmanship. They run in front of elephants, run in front of horses, run in front of chariots, and they run after them. They shout, clap their hands, wrestle, and box with their fists. They spread their outer robe in the middle of an arena and say to a dancing girl, ‘Dance here, sister,’ and they make gestures with their foreheads. They engage in various other improper kinds of conduct. This, bhikkhus, is not for the conviction of the unconvicted… Having rebuked them… he gave a Dhamma talk and then addressed Sāriputta and Moggallāna: “Go, Sāriputta, go, Moggallāna, to Kīṭāgiri and carry out the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu, expelling them from Kīṭāgiri. They are your co-dwellers.”

‘‘Kathaṃ mayaṃ, bhante, assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ karoma, caṇḍā te bhikkhū pharusā’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tumhe, sāriputtā, bahukehi bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ gacchathā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho sāriputtamoggallānā bhagavato paccassosuṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ – paṭhamaṃ assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū codetabbā, codetvā sāretabbā, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbā, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

“Bhante, how should we perform the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri? Those bhikkhus are fierce and rough.” “Then, Sāriputta, you should go with many bhikkhus.” “Yes, Bhante,” Sāriputta and Moggallāna replied to the Blessed One. And this, bhikkhus, is how it should be done: first, the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should be charged, then reminded, then charged with an offense. After charging them with an offense, a competent and capable bhikkhu should inform the Saṅgha:

24. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū kuladūsakā pāpasamācārā. Imesaṃ pāpakā samācārā dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Kulāni ca imehi duṭṭhāni dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti. Esā ñatti.

24.“Bhante, may the Saṅgha hear me. These bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu are corrupters of families, of evil conduct. Their evil conduct is seen and heard, and the families corrupted by them are seen and heard. If the Saṅgha is ready, the Saṅgha should perform the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri, to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū kuladūsakā pāpasamācārā. Imesaṃ pāpakā samācārā dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Kulāni ca imehi duṭṭhāni dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Saṅgho assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ karoti – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti. Yassāyasmato khamati assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“Bhante, may the Saṅgha hear me. These bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu are corrupters of families, of evil conduct. Their evil conduct is seen and heard, and the families corrupted by them are seen and heard. The Saṅgha performs the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri, to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri. Any venerable one who approves of the Saṅgha’s performance of the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri—to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri—should remain silent. Any venerable one who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi. Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ime assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū kuladūsakā pāpasamācārā. Imesaṃ pāpakā samācārā dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Kulāni ca imehi duṭṭhāni dissanti ceva suyyanti ca. Saṅgho assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ karoti – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti. Yassāyasmato khamati assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“For the second time I state this matter… For the third time I state this matter. Bhante, may the Saṅgha hear me. These bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu are corrupters of families, of evil conduct. Their evil conduct is seen and heard, and the families corrupted by them are seen and heard. The Saṅgha performs the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri, to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri. Any venerable one who approves of the Saṅgha’s performance of the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri—to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri—should remain silent. Any venerable one who does not approve should speak.”

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

“The Saṅgha has performed the act of expulsion against the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu from Kīṭāgiri, to the effect that the bhikkhus Assaji and Punabbasu should not dwell in Kīṭāgiri. The Saṅgha assents to it, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.”

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelvefold Unlawful Acts

25. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

25.“Monks, an act of expulsion endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, an undisciplinary act, and badly settled. It is done not in the presence [of the accused], done without questioning, done without acknowledgment—an act of expulsion endowed with these three factors, monks, is an unlawful act, an undisciplinary act, and badly settled.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti …pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

“Furthermore, monks, an act of expulsion endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, an undisciplinary act, and badly settled. It is done when there is no offense, done for an offense that does not lead to confession, done for an offense that has been confessed... done without accusation, done without inquiry, done without the offense being established... done not in the presence [of the accused], done unlawfully, done by a faction... done without questioning, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done without acknowledgment, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done when there is no offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done for an offense that does not lead to confession, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done for an offense that has been confessed, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done without accusation, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done without inquiry, done unlawfully, done by a faction... done without the offense being established, done unlawfully, done by a faction—monks, an act of expulsion endowed with these three factors is an unlawful act, an undisciplinary act, and badly settled.”

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Twelvefold Unlawful Acts is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelve Lawful Acts.

26. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

26.Monks, an expulsion endowed with three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well settled. It is done in the presence, done with questioning, and done with acknowledgment. Monks, an expulsion endowed with these three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well settled.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ pabbājanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an expulsion endowed with three other factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well settled. It is done regarding an offense, done regarding an offense that requires confession, done regarding an unconfessed offense... done having charged, done having reminded, done having imputed an offense... done in the presence, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done with questioning, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done with acknowledgment, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done regarding an offense, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done regarding an offense that requires confession, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done regarding an unconfessed offense, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done having charged, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done having reminded, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly... done having imputed an offense, done lawfully, done by a complete assembly—monks, an expulsion endowed with these three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well settled.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Twelve Lawful Acts are concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānacuddasakaṃ

The Fourteenfold on Account of Desire.

27. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

27.Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, verbose, and a maker of legal issues in the Saṅgha; he is foolish, incompetent, full of offenses, and unrepentant; he lives in association with householders in unbecoming ways. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is corrupted in higher virtue, corrupted in conduct, corrupted in view. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He speaks dispraise of the Buddha, speaks dispraise of the Dhamma, speaks dispraise of the Saṅgha. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Kāyikena davena samannāgato hoti, vācasikena davena samannāgato hoti, kāyikavācasikena davena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is endowed with bodily indulgence, endowed with verbal indulgence, endowed with bodily and verbal indulgence. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Kāyikena anācārena samannāgato hoti, vācasikena anācārena samannāgato hoti, kāyikavācasikena anācārena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is endowed with bodily misconduct, endowed with verbal misconduct, endowed with bodily and verbal misconduct. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Kāyikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti, vācasikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti, kāyikavācasikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is endowed with bodily harmfulness, endowed with verbal harmfulness, endowed with bodily and verbal harmfulness. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Kāyikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti, vācasikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti, kāyikavācasikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti – imehi, kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with three other qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment. He is endowed with bodily wrong livelihood, endowed with verbal wrong livelihood, endowed with bodily and verbal wrong livelihood. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities—if the Saṅgha wishes—may be subjected to an act of banishment.

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, verbose, and a maker of legal issues in the Saṅgha; one is foolish, incompetent, full of offenses, and unrepentant; one lives in association with householders in unbecoming ways. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is corrupted in higher virtue, one is corrupted in conduct, one is corrupted in view. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One speaks dispraise of the Buddha, one speaks dispraise of the Dhamma, one speaks dispraise of the Saṅgha. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko kāyikena davena samannāgato hoti, eko vācasikena davena samannāgato hoti, eko kāyikavācasikena davena samannāgato hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is endowed with bodily indulgence, one is endowed with verbal indulgence, one is endowed with bodily and verbal indulgence. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko kāyikena anācārena samannāgato hoti, eko vācasikena anācārena samannāgato hoti, eko kāyikavācasikena anācārena samannāgato hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is endowed with bodily misconduct, one is endowed with verbal misconduct, one is endowed with bodily and verbal misconduct. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko kāyikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti, eko vācasikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti, eko kāyikavācasikena upaghātikena samannāgato hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is endowed with bodily harmfulness, one is endowed with verbal harmfulness, one is endowed with bodily and verbal harmfulness. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko kāyikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti, eko vācasikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti, eko kāyikavācasikena micchājīvena samannāgato hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pabbājanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject three other bhikkhus to an act of banishment. One is endowed with bodily wrong livelihood, one is endowed with verbal wrong livelihood, one is endowed with bodily and verbal wrong livelihood. Monks, the Saṅgha—if it wishes—may subject these three bhikkhus to an act of banishment.

Ākaṅkhamānacuddasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Fourteenfold on Account of Desire is concluded.

Aṭṭhārasavattaṃ

Eighteen Observances

28. ‘‘Pabbājanīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena pabbājanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

28.“Monks, a monk against whom an act of banishment has been carried out must conduct himself properly. And what is proper conduct in this case? He must not confer ordination, he must not grant dependence, he must not have a novice attend him, he must not accept appointment as an instructor for nuns, and even if appointed, he must not instruct nuns. He must not commit the offense for which the Sangha carried out the act of banishment, nor another similar to it, nor one even worse. He must not disparage the act, nor must he disparage those who carried it out. He must not prevent a fully established monk’s observance of the Uposatha, nor his Pavāraṇā; he must not make a declaration; he must not make an accusation; he must not create an opportunity (for accusation); he must not accuse; he must not remind; and he must not associate with monks.”

Pabbājanīyakamme aṭṭhārasavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen observances concerning the act of banishment are concluded.

29. Atha kho sāriputtamoggallānappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho kīṭāgiriṃ gantvā assajipunabbasukānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kīṭāgirismā pabbājanīyakammaṃ akāsi – na assajipunabbasukehi bhikkhūhi kīṭāgirismiṃ vatthabbanti. Te saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakatā na sammā vattanti, na lomaṃ pātenti, na netthāraṃ vattanti; na bhikkhū khamāpenti, akkosanti, paribhāsanti; chandagāmitā dosagāmitā mohagāmitā bhayagāmitā pāpenti; pakkamantipi, vibbhamantipi. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakatā na sammā vattissanti, na lomaṃ pātessanti, na netthāraṃ vattissanti; na bhikkhū khamāpessanti, akkosissanti, paribhāsissanti; chandagāmitā dosagāmitā mohagāmitā bhayagāmitā pāpessanti; pakkamissantipi, vibbhamissantipī’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

29.Then the Sangha of monks, with Sāriputta and Moggallāna at their head, went to Kīṭāgiri and carried out an act of banishment against the monks Assaji and Punabbasuka, (decreeing) 'The monks Assaji and Punabbasuka must not dwell in Kīṭāgiri.' But those monks, against whom the Sangha had carried out the act of banishment, did not conduct themselves properly, did not humble themselves, did not act for their own good; they did not ask forgiveness of the monks, but instead insulted and reviled them; they gave way to partiality, hostility, delusion, and fear; and they departed and roamed about. Those monks who were of few desires… complained and criticized, saying, “How can the monks Assaji and Punabbasuka, against whom the Sangha has carried out the act of banishment, not conduct themselves properly, not humble themselves, not act for their own good; not ask forgiveness of the monks, but instead insult and revile them; give way to partiality, hostility, delusion, and fear; and depart and roam about?” Then those monks informed the Blessed One of this matter.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, assajipunabbasukā bhikkhū saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakatā na sammā vattanti, na lomaṃ pātenti, na netthāraṃ vattanti; na bhikkhū khamāpenti, akkosanti, paribhāsanti; chandagāmitā dosagāmitā mohagāmitā bhayagāmitā pāpenti; pakkamantipi, vibbhamantipī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ …pe… kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakatā na sammā vattissanti, na lomaṃ pātessanti, na netthāraṃ vattissanti; na bhikkhū khamāpessanti, akkosissanti, paribhāsissanti; chandagāmitā dosagāmitā mohagāmitā bhayagāmitā pāpessanti; pakkamissantipi, vibbhamissantipi. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

The Blessed One then, on this occasion, because of this matter, had the Sangha of monks assembled, and questioned the monks: “Is it true, monks, that the monks Assaji and Punabbasuka, against whom the Sangha has carried out the act of banishment, do not conduct themselves properly, do not humble themselves, do not act for their own good; do not ask forgiveness of the monks, but insult and revile them, and give way to partiality, hostility, delusion, and fear; and they depart and wander about?” “It is true, Blessed One.” The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked them: “It is unsuitable… How indeed, monks, can these foolish men, against whom the Sangha has carried out the act of banishment, not conduct themselves properly, not humble themselves, not act for their own good; not ask forgiveness of the monks, but insult and revile them, and give way to partiality, hostility, delusion, and fear; and depart and wander about? This will not lead to confidence in the unconvinced….” After rebuking them… having given a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: “Then, monks, let the Sangha revoke the act of banishment.”

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The eighteen instances where it should not be rescinded.

30. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

30.Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should not have the banishment act rescinded. He gives ordination, he gives dependence, he has a novice attend on him, he approves the appointment as an instructor of nuns, and even if appointed, he instructs nuns—a monk endowed with these five factors should not have the banishment act rescinded.

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena pabbājanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with another five factors should not be rescinded. He commits the same offense for which the Sangha carried out the banishment act, or one similar to it, or even worse; he disparages the act, he disparages those who carried out the act—monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with these five factors should not be rescinded.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with eight factors should not be rescinded. He suspends the Uposatha of a normal monk, he suspends the Pavāraṇā, he makes himself open to admonition, he initiates a formal charge, he requests an opportunity, he accuses, he reminds, and he causes monks to associate (with him)—monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with these eight factors should not be rescinded.

Pabbājanīyakamme nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen instances concerning the banishment act that should not be rescinded are concluded.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The eighteen instances where it should be rescinded.

31. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

31.Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should have the banishment act rescinded. He does not give ordination, he does not give dependence, he does not have a novice attend on him, he does not approve the appointment as an instructor of nuns, and even if appointed, he does not instruct nuns—a monk endowed with these five factors should have the banishment act rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena pabbājanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with another five factors should be rescinded. He does not commit the same offense for which the Sangha carried out the banishment act, nor another similar to it, nor one worse than it; he does not disparage the act, he does not disparage those who carried out the act—monks, the banishment act against a monk endowed with these five factors should be rescinded.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, a monk endowed with eight factors should have the banishment act rescinded. He does not suspend the Uposatha of a normal monk, he does not suspend the Pavāraṇā, he does not make himself open to admonition, he does not initiate a formal charge, he does not request an opportunity, he does not accuse, he does not remind, and he does not cause monks to associate (with him)—a monk endowed with these eight factors should have the banishment act rescinded.

Pabbājanīyakamme paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen cases where the banishment act is to be rescinded are concluded.

32. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena, bhikkhave, pabbājanīyakammakatena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

32.And, monks, it should be rescinded in this way. The monk who has been subjected to the banishment act should approach the Sangha, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior monks, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined palms, and say this: 'Venerable sirs, I have been subjected to the banishment act by the Sangha. I am behaving properly, I am letting down my hair, I am conducting myself so as to be drawn out (of the fault). I request the rescinding of the banishment act.' He should request a second time. He should request a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Sangha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk, named so-and-so, who has been subjected to the banishment act by the Sangha, is behaving properly, has let down his hair, is conducting himself so as to be drawn out (of the fault), and requests the rescinding of the banishment act. If it is agreeable to the Sangha, may the Sangha rescind the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so. This is the announcement.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk, named so-and-so, upon whom the Sangha has carried out the banishment act, is behaving properly, has let down his hair, is conducting himself so as to be drawn out (of the fault), and requests the rescinding of the banishment act. The Sangha rescinds the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so. To whomever it is agreeable that the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so be rescinded, let him be silent; to whomever it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi. Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena pabbājanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

I speak on this matter a second time... I speak on this matter a third time. Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk, named so-and-so, who has been subjected to the banishment act by the Sangha, is behaving properly, has let down his hair, is conducting himself so as to be drawn out (of the fault), and requests the rescinding of the banishment act. The Sangha rescinds the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so. To whomever it is agreeable that the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so be rescinded, let him be silent; to whomever it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena itthannāmassa bhikkhuno pabbājanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā

The Sangha has rescinded the banishment act for the monk named so-and-so. It is agreeable to the Sangha, therefore

Tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

Silent, thus I hold it.

Pabbājanīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ tatiyaṃ.

The banishment act is concluded, the third.

### 4. Paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ - Act of Reconciliation ^4

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^4|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.4" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


33. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā sudhammo macchikāsaṇḍe cittassa gahapatino āvāsiko hoti, navakammiko dhuvabhattiko. Yadā citto gahapati saṅghaṃ vā gaṇaṃ vā puggalaṃ vā nimantetukāmo hoti tadā na āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ anapaloketvā saṅghaṃ vā gaṇaṃ vā puggalaṃ vā nimanteti.

33.At that time, Venerable Sudhamma was residing in Macchikāsaṇḍa, dwelling in dependence on the householder Citta, performing new construction work and receiving regular meals. Whenever the householder Citta wished to invite the Saṅgha, a group, or an individual, he would not invite the Saṅgha, a group, or an individual without first consulting Venerable Sudhamma.

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā therā bhikkhū, āyasmā ca sāriputto, āyasmā ca mahāmoggallāno, āyasmā ca mahākaccāno, āyasmā ca mahākoṭṭhiko, āyasmā ca mahākappino, āyasmā ca mahācundo, āyasmā ca anuruddho, āyasmā ca revato, āyasmā ca upāli, āyasmā ca ānando, āyasmā ca rāhulo, kāsīsu cārikaṃ caramānā yena macchikāsaṇḍo tadavasaruṃ.

At that time, a number of senior monks—Venerable Sāriputta, Venerable Mahāmoggallāna, Venerable Mahākaccāna, Venerable Mahākoṭṭhita, Venerable Mahākappina, Venerable Mahācunda, Venerable Anuruddha, Venerable Revata, Venerable Upāli, Venerable Ānanda, and Venerable Rāhula—wandering on tour in the Kāsi country, arrived at Macchikāsaṇḍa.

Assosi kho citto gahapati therā kira bhikkhū macchikāsaṇḍaṃ anuppattāti. Atha kho citto gahapati yena therā bhikkhū tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā there bhikkhū abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho cittaṃ gahapatiṃ āyasmā sāriputto dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi.

Citta the householder heard that elder monks had arrived at Macchikāsaṇḍa. Then Citta the householder approached the elder monks, and after paying homage to them, sat down to one side. As he sat to one side, Venerable Sāriputta instructed, roused, inspired, and gladdened Citta the householder with a Dhamma talk.

Atha kho citto gahapati āyasmatā sāriputtena dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito there bhikkhū etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsentu me, bhante, therā svātanāya āgantukabhatta’’nti. Adhivāsesuṃ kho therā bhikkhū [adhivāsesuṃ kho te therā bhikkhū (syā.)] tuṇhībhāvena.

Then the householder Citta, having been shown, roused, inspired, and gladdened by Venerable Sāriputta with a Dhamma talk, said this to the elder monks: "Venerable sirs, may the elders consent to a meal from me tomorrow for newly arrived monks." The elder monks consented by remaining silent.

Atha kho citto gahapati therānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā there bhikkhū abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā yenāyasmā sudhammo tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho citto gahapati āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, ayyo sudhammo svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ therehī’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā sudhammo ‘pubbe khvāyaṃ citto gahapati yadā saṅghaṃ vā gaṇaṃ vā puggalaṃ vā nimantetukāmo na maṃ anapaloketvā saṅghaṃ vā gaṇaṃ vā puggalaṃ vā nimanteti; sodāni maṃ anapaloketvā there bhikkhū nimantesi; duṭṭhodānāyaṃ citto gahapati anapekkho virattarūpo mayī’ti cittaṃ gahapatiṃ etadavoca – ‘‘alaṃ, gahapati, nādhivāsemī’’ti. Dutiyampi kho…pe… tatiyampi kho citto gahapati āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, ayyo sudhammo svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ therehī’’ti. ‘‘Alaṃ, gahapati, nādhivāsemī’’ti. Atha kho citto gahapati ‘kiṃ me karissati ayyo sudhammo adhivāsento vā anadhivāsento vā’ti āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

Then the householder Citta, understanding the elder monks' acceptance, rose from his seat, paid homage to the elder monks, circumambulated them, and approached the Venerable Sudhamma. Having approached, he paid homage to the Venerable Sudhamma and stood to one side. Standing to one side, the householder Citta said to the Venerable Sudhamma: "Venerable Sir, may the Venerable Sudhamma accept my invitation for tomorrow's meal together with the elder monks." Then the Venerable Sudhamma thought: "Previously, this householder Citta, whenever he wished to invite the Saṅgha, a group, or an individual, would not invite the Saṅgha, a group, or an individual without consulting me. But now he invites the elder monks without consulting me. This householder Citta is surely displeased, without regard for, and estranged from me." He said to the householder Citta: "Enough, householder, I will not accept." A second time... a third time the householder Citta said to the Venerable Sudhamma: "Venerable Sir, may the Venerable Sudhamma accept my invitation for tomorrow's meal together with the elder monks." "Enough, householder, I will not accept." Then the householder Citta thought: "What can the Venerable Sudhamma do to me, whether he accepts or does not accept?" He paid homage to the Venerable Sudhamma, circumambulated him, and departed.

34. Atha kho citto gahapati tassā rattiyā accayena therānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpesi. Atha kho āyasmā sudhammo ‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ cittassa gahapatino therānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ paṭiyattaṃ passeyya’nti pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena cittassa gahapatino nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Atha kho citto gahapati yenāyasmā sudhammo tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ sudhammaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho cittaṃ gahapatiṃ āyasmā sudhammo etadavoca – ‘‘pahūtaṃ kho te idaṃ, gahapati, khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyattaṃ; ekā ca kho idha natthi yadidaṃ tilasaṅguḷikā’’ti. ‘‘Bahumhi vata, bhante, ratane buddhavacane [bhante buddhavacane (syā.)] vijjamāne ayyena sudhammena yadeva kiñci bhāsitaṃ yadidaṃ tilasaṅguḷikāti. Bhūtapubbaṃ, bhante, dakkhiṇāpathakā vāṇijā puratthimaṃ janapadaṃ agamaṃsu vāṇijjāya. Te tato kukkuṭiṃ ānesuṃ. Atha kho sā, bhante, kukkuṭī kākena saddhiṃ saṃvāsaṃ kappesi. Sā potakaṃ janesi. Yadā kho so, bhante, kukkuṭapotako kākavassaṃ vassitukāmo hoti, kākakukkuṭīti vassati; yadā kukkuṭivassaṃ vassitukāmo hoti, kukkuṭikākāti vassati. Evameva kho, bhante, bahumhi ratane buddhavacane vijjamāne ayyena sudhammena yadeva kiñci bhāsitaṃ yadidaṃ tilasaṃguḷikā’’ti. ‘‘Akkosasi maṃ tvaṃ, gahapati, paribhāsasi maṃ tvaṃ, gahapati. Eso te, gahapati, āvāso, pakkamissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Nāhaṃ, bhante, ayyaṃ sudhammaṃ akkosāmi, paribhāsāmi [na paribhāsāmi (sī. syā.)]. Vasatu, bhante, ayyo sudhammo macchikāsaṇḍe. Ramaṇīyaṃ ambāṭakavanaṃ. Ahaṃ ayyassa sudhammassa ussukkaṃ karissāmi, cīvarapiṇḍapātasenāsanagilānappaccayabhesajjaparikkhārāna’’nti. Dutiyampi kho…pe… tatiyampi kho āyasmā sudhammo cittaṃ gahapatiṃ etadavoca – ‘‘akkosasi maṃ tvaṃ, gahapati, paribhāsasi maṃ tvaṃ, gahapati. Eso te, gahapati, āvāso, pakkamissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Kahaṃ, bhante, ayyo sudhammo gamissatī’’ti? ‘‘Sāvatthiṃ kho ahaṃ, gahapati, gamissāmi bhagavantaṃ dassanāyā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, bhante, yañca attanā bhaṇitaṃ, yañca mayā bhaṇitaṃ taṃ sabbaṃ bhagavato ārocehi. Anacchariyaṃ kho panetaṃ, bhante, yaṃ ayyo sudhammo punadeva macchikāsaṇḍaṃ paccāgaccheyyā’’ti.

34.Then, after the night had passed, the householder Citta prepared excellent hard and soft food for the elder monks. Then Venerable Sudhamma thought, "Why don't I see what the householder Citta has prepared for the elder monks?" So in the morning, having dressed, taken his bowl and robe, he went to the dwelling of the householder Citta. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat. Then the householder Citta approached Venerable Sudhamma, paid respects to him, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, Venerable Sudhamma said to him: "Householder, you have prepared a great deal of hard and soft food here, but there is one thing missing—sesame cakes." "Venerable sir, though there is much treasure in the Buddha's words, Venerable Sudhamma speaks only of sesame cakes. Once, sir, merchants from the Southern region went to the Eastern lands for trade. They brought back a hen. That hen, sir, engaged in intercourse with a crow and produced a chick. When that chick, sir, wanted to make a crow's sound, it would sound 'crow-hen'; when it wanted to make a hen's sound, it would sound 'hen-crow.' In the same way, sir, though there is much treasure in the Buddha's words, Venerable Sudhamma speaks only of sesame cakes." "Householder, you insult me! You revile me! This is your dwelling—I will leave!" "I do not insult or revile Venerable Sudhamma. Let Venerable Sudhamma stay in Macchikāsaṇḍa. The mango grove is delightful. I will attend to Venerable Sudhamma’s needs—robes, almsfood, lodging, and medicine." A second time... a third time, Venerable Sudhamma said to the householder Citta: "Householder, you insult me! You revile me! This is your dwelling—I will leave!" "Where will Venerable Sudhamma go, sir?" "I will go to Sāvatthī, householder, to see the Blessed One." "Then, sir, please report to the Blessed One both what you have said and what I have said. It would not be a surprise, sir, if Venerable Sudhamma were to return to Macchikāsaṇḍa."

35. Atha kho āyasmā sudhammo senāsanaṃ saṃsāmetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena sāvatthi tena pakkāmi. Anupubbena yena sāvatthi jetavanaṃ anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāmo yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho āyasmā sudhammo yañca attanā bhaṇitaṃ yañca cittena gahapatinā bhaṇitaṃ taṃ sabbaṃ bhagavato ārocesi.

35.Then Venerable Sudhamma, having put his dwelling in order and taking his bowl and robe, set out for Savatthi. In due course, he arrived at Savatthi, at Jeta's Grove, Anathapindika's monastery, and approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Seated to one side, Venerable Sudhamma reported to the Blessed One all that he had said and all that the householder had said.

Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, moghapurisa, ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, cittaṃ gahapatiṃ saddhaṃ pasannaṃ dāyakaṃ kārakaṃ saṅghupaṭṭhākaṃ hīnena khuṃsessasi, hīnena vambhessasi? Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ karotu – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ – paṭhamaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu codetabbo, codetvā sāretabbo, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbo, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

The Blessed One rebuked him: "Foolish man, this is unseemly, unsuitable, inappropriate, unworthy of an ascetic, unbecoming, and not to be done. How could you, foolish man, humiliate and disparage the householder Citta, who is faithful, devoted, a donor, a benefactor, and a regular attendant of the Saṅgha, in a base manner? This, foolish man, does not conduce to the confidence of the unconfident…" Having rebuked him… he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Well then, monks, let the Saṅgha perform the act of reconciliation towards the monk Sudhamma—'Citta the householder must be asked to forgive you.' And this, monks, is how it should be done: First, the monk Sudhamma should be charged, then reminded, then the offense should be imposed, and then a competent monk should inform the Saṅgha:

36. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu cittaṃ gahapatiṃ saddhaṃ pasannaṃ dāyakaṃ kārakaṃ saṅghupaṭṭhākaṃ hīnena khuṃseti, hīnena vambheti. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti. Esā ñatti.

36."Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma insults and disparages the householder Citta—who is faithful, devoted, a donor, a supporter, and a regular attendant of the Saṅgha—in a base manner. If the Saṅgha is ready, let the Saṅgha perform the act of bringing Sudhamma bhikkhu to reconciliation—[with the instruction] 'You must ask forgiveness of the householder Citta.' This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu cittaṃ gahapatiṃ saddhaṃ pasannaṃ dāyakaṃ kārakaṃ saṅghupaṭṭhākaṃ hīnena khuṃseti, hīnena vambheti. Saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ karoti – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti. Yassāyasmato khamati sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma insults and disparages Citta the householder—who is faithful, devoted, a donor, a benefactor, and an attendant of the Saṅgha—in a base manner. The Saṅgha performs the act of reconciliation for the monk Sudhamma—'You must ask forgiveness of Citta the householder.' If it is agreeable to the venerable ones that the act of reconciliation be performed for the monk Sudhamma—'You must ask forgiveness of Citta the householder'—let them remain silent. If it is not agreeable, let them speak."

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu cittaṃ gahapatiṃ saddhaṃ pasannaṃ dāyakaṃ kārakaṃ saṅghupaṭṭhākaṃ hīnena khuṃseti, hīnena vambheti. Saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ karoti – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti. Yassāyasmato khamati sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"For the second time, I speak on this matter… For the third time, I speak on this matter: Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma insults and disparages the householder Citta—who is faithful, devoted, a donor, a benefactor, and a regular attendant of the Saṅgha—in a base manner. The Saṅgha performs the act of reconciliation for the monk Sudhamma—‘You must seek forgiveness from the householder Citta.’ If it is agreeable to the venerable ones that the act of reconciliation be performed for the monk Sudhamma—‘You must seek forgiveness from the householder Citta’—then remain silent. If it does not please you, speak up."

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ – citto te gahapati khamāpetabboti. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

"The Saṅgha has performed the act of reconciliation regarding the monk Sudhamma—'Citta the householder must be asked for forgiveness.' It is agreeable to the Saṅgha, therefore they are silent. Thus I hold it."

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelve Unlawful Actions

37. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

37.“Monks, an act of reconciliation endowed with three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled. It is done not in the presence (of the accused), without questioning, and without admission. Monks, an act of reconciliation endowed with these three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

“Furthermore, monks, an act of reconciliation endowed with these other three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled.
