It is done when there is no offense; it is done for an offense that does not lead to confession; it is done for an offense that has been confessed… it is done without accusation; it is done without investigation; it is done without formally charging an offense… it is done not in the presence (of the accused), unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done without questioning, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done without admission, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done when there is no offense, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done for an offense that does not lead to confession, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done for an offense that has been confessed, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done without accusation, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done without investigation, unlawfully, and by a faction… it is done without formally charging an offense, unlawfully, and by a faction. Monks, an act of reconciliation endowed with these three factors is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled.”

Paṭisāraṇīyakamme adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on the Twelve Unlawful Actions Concerning the Act of Reconciliation is Concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The twelvefold lawful act.

38. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

38."Monks, a reconciliation procedure endowed with three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well concluded. It is done face to face, done with questioning, done upon acknowledgment—monks, a reconciliation procedure endowed with these three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well concluded."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a reconciliation procedure endowed with three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well concluded. It is done regarding an offense, done regarding an offense that requires confession, done regarding an offense that has not been confessed… done with accusation, done with reminding, done with charging an offense… done face-to-face, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done with questioning, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done with acknowledgment, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done regarding an offense, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done regarding an offense that requires confession, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done regarding an offense that has not been confessed, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done with accusation, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done with reminding, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha… done with charging an offense, done according to the Dhamma, done by a complete Saṅgha—monks, a reconciliation procedure endowed with these three factors is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well concluded."

Paṭisāraṇīyakamme dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The twelvefold lawful act concerning the act of reconciliation is concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānacatukkaṃ

The Fours on Wishing

39. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya. Gihīnaṃ alābhāya parisakkati, gihīnaṃ anatthāya parisakkati, gihīnaṃ anāvāsāya [avāsāya (sī.)] parisakkati, gihī akkosati paribhāsati, gihī gihīhi bhedeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya.

39.“Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against a bhikkhu endowed with five qualities. He strives for the non-gain of householders, strives for the disadvantage of householders, strives for the non-dwelling of householders, insults and reviles householders, and divides householders among themselves. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya. Gihīnaṃ buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, gihīnaṃ dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, gihīnaṃ saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, gihī hīnena khuṃseti hīnena vambheti, gihīnaṃ dhammikaṃ paṭissavaṃ na saccāpeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya.

“Furthermore, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities. He speaks dispraise of the Buddha to householders, speaks dispraise of the Dhamma to householders, speaks dispraise of the Saṅgha to householders, reviles and disparages householders with base speech, and does not make true a legitimate promise to householders. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities.”

‘‘Pañcannaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko gihīnaṃ alābhāya parisakkati, eko gihīnaṃ anatthāya parisakkati, eko gihīnaṃ anāvāsāya parisakkati, eko gihī akkosati paribhāsati, eko gihī gihīhi bhedeti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, pañcannaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya.

“Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against five bhikkhus. One strives for the non-gain of householders; one strives for the disadvantage of householders; one strives for the non-dwelling of householders; one insults and reviles householders; and one divides householders among themselves. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against these five bhikkhus.”

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, pañcannaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko gihīnaṃ buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko gihīnaṃ dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko gihīnaṃ saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko gihī hīnena khuṃseti hīnena vambheti, eko gihīnaṃ dhammikaṃ paṭissavaṃ na saccāpeti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, pañcannaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kareyya.

“Furthermore, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against five other bhikkhus. One speaks dispraise of the Buddha to householders; one speaks dispraise of the Dhamma to householders; one speaks dispraise of the Saṅgha to householders; one reviles and disparages householders with base speech; and one does not make true a legitimate promise to householders. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may perform an act of reconciliation against these five bhikkhus.”

Ākaṅkhamānacatukkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Fours on Wishing are concluded.

Aṭṭhārasavattaṃ

Eighteen Rules of Conduct.

40. ‘‘Paṭisāraṇīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

40.Monks, a monk against whom an act of reconciliation has been performed must conduct himself properly. And what is proper conduct in this case? He should not confer ordination, he should not grant dependence, he should not have a novice wait upon him, he should not solicit agreement to be appointed to instruct nuns, and even if appointed, he should not instruct nuns. He should not commit the offense for which the Sangha performed the act of reconciliation, nor another like it, nor one still more serious. He should not disparage the act, nor should he disparage those who performed it. He should not prevent a qualified monk from observing the Uposatha, nor from observing the Pavāraṇā, nor should he make a verbal challenge, nor should he initiate a formal charge, nor should he request a hearing, nor should he accuse, nor should he remind, nor should he conspire with monks.

Paṭisāraṇīyakamme aṭṭhārasavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eighteen-point reconciliation procedure is concluded.

41. Atha kho saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ akāsi – ‘‘citto te gahapati khamāpetabbo’’ti. So saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato macchikāsaṇḍaṃ gantvā maṅkubhūto nāsakkhi cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ. Punadeva sāvatthiṃ paccāgañchi. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘khamāpito tayā, āvuso sudhamma, citto gahapatī’’ti? ‘‘Idhāhaṃ, āvuso, macchikāsaṇḍaṃ gantvā maṅkubhūto nāsakkhiṃ cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetu’’nti. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe…. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno anudūtaṃ detu – cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ. Evañca pana bhikkhave dātabbo – paṭhamaṃ bhikkhu yācitabbo, yācitvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

41.Then the Sangha performed the act of prompting repentance for the monk Sudhamma: "The householder Citta must be asked for forgiveness." Having been subjected to the act of prompting repentance by the Sangha, he went to Macchikāsaṇḍa but, being humiliated, was unable to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness. He returned again to Sāvatthī. The monks asked him, "Friend Sudhamma, have you asked the householder Citta for forgiveness?" "Friends, after going to Macchikāsaṇḍa, I was humiliated and unable to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness." The monks informed the Blessed One of the matter… "Well then, monks, let the Sangha appoint a deputy for the monk Sudhamma to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness. And this is how it should be done: First, a monk should be requested. Having requested him, a competent and able monk should inform the Sangha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmaṃ bhikkhuṃ sudhammassa bhikkhuno anudūtaṃ dadeyya cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ. Esā ñatti.

"Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. If the Sangha is ready, the Sangha may give such-and-such a monk as a deputy for the monk Sudhamma to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ bhikkhuṃ sudhammassa bhikkhuno anudūtaṃ deti cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno sudhammassa bhikkhuno anudūtassa dānaṃ cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable Sirs, let the Saṅgha hear me. The Saṅgha gives such-and-such a bhikkhu as a deputy to the bhikkhu Sudhamma to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness. If it is acceptable to the venerable ones that such-and-such a bhikkhu be given as a deputy to the bhikkhu Sudhamma to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness, let them remain silent; if it is not acceptable, let them speak."

‘‘Dinno saṅghena itthannāmo bhikkhu sudhammassa bhikkhuno anudūto cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpetuṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

"The Sangha has appointed the monk named so-and-so as a deputy for the monk Sudhamma to ask the householder Citta for forgiveness. It is acceptable to the Sangha, therefore they are silent. Thus I hold it."

42. ‘‘Tena, bhikkhave, sudhammena bhikkhunā anudūtena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ macchikāsaṇḍaṃ gantvā citto gahapati khamāpetabbo – ‘khama, gahapati, pasādemi ta’nti. Evañce vuccamāno khamati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce khamati, anudūtena bhikkhunā vattabbo – ‘khama, gahapati, imassa bhikkhuno, pasādeti ta’nti. Evañce vuccamāno khamati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce khamati, anudūtena bhikkhunā vattabbo – ‘khama, gahapati, imassa bhikkhuno, ahaṃ taṃ pasādemī’ti. Evañce vuccamāno khamati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce khamati, anudūtena bhikkhunā vattabbo – ‘khama, gahapati, imassa bhikkhuno, saṅghassa vacanenā’ti. Evañce vuccamāno khamati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce khamati, anudūtena bhikkhunā sudhammo bhikkhu [sudhammaṃ bhikkhuṃ… sā āpatti desāpetabbāti (sī. syā.)] cittassa gahapatino dassanūpacāraṃ avijahāpetvā savanūpacāraṃ avijahāpetvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā taṃ āpattiṃ desāpetabbo’’ti [sudhammaṃ bhikkhuṃ… sā āpatti desāpetabbāti (sī. syā.)].

42."Then, monks, the monk Sudhamma, accompanied by the deputy monk, should go to Macchikāsaṇḍa and ask the householder Citta for forgiveness: 'Forgive me, householder, I seek your appeasement.' If, being spoken to thus, he forgives, that is skillful. If he does not forgive, the deputy monk should say: 'Forgive, householder, this monk, he seeks your appeasement.' If, being spoken to thus, he forgives, that is skillful. If he does not forgive, the deputy monk should say: 'Forgive, householder, this monk; I seek your appeasement on his behalf.' If, being spoken to thus, he forgives, that is skillful. If he does not forgive, the deputy monk should say: 'Forgive, householder, this monk, by the word of the Sangha.' If, being spoken to thus, he forgives, that is skillful. If he does not forgive, the deputy monk should have the monk Sudhamma, without relinquishing the householder Citta's sight or hearing, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, sit on his heels, raise his hands in añjali, and confess the offense."

Atha kho āyasmā sudhammo anudūtena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ macchikāsaṇḍaṃ gantvā cittaṃ gahapatiṃ khamāpesi. So sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘ahaṃ, āvuso, saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… ‘‘tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

Then the Venerable Sudhamma, together with the deputy monk, went to Macchikāsaṇḍa and sought forgiveness from the householder Citta. He behaved properly, showed remorse, and behaved irreproachably. He approached the monks and said: “Friends, having been subjected to a procedure requiring reconciliation by the Sangha, I behave properly, show remorse, and behave irreproachably. How should I proceed?” The monks reported this matter to the Blessed One… “Well then, monks, let the Sangha rescind the procedure requiring reconciliation for the monk Sudhamma.

Nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The Eighteen Not to Be Rescinded

43. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

43.“Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with five factors. He confers the Going Forth, he gives dependence, he has a novice attend on him, he approves the appointment as an advisor of nuns, and even when appointed, he advises nuns. Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with these five factors.”

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

“Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with another five factors. He commits the offense for which the Saṅgha performed the act requiring amends, or another similar to it, or one worse than it; he disparages the act, he disparages those who performed it. Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with these five factors.”

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ’’.

“Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with eight factors. He suspends the Uposatha of a monk in good standing, he suspends the Pavāraṇā, he makes himself difficult to speak to, he establishes grounds for accusation, he makes an opportunity, he accuses, he reminds, and he associates with monks. Monks, the act requiring amends should not be rescinded for a monk endowed with these eight factors.”

Paṭisāraṇīyakamme nappaṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on the Eighteen Not to Be Rescinded Regarding the Act Requiring Amends is Concluded.

Paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ

The Eighteen to Be Rescinded

44. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

44.“Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with five factors. He does not confer the Going Forth, he does not give dependence, he does not have a novice attend on him, he does not approve the appointment as an advisor of nuns, and even when appointed, he does not advise nuns. Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with these five factors.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

“Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with another five factors. He does not commit the offense for which the Saṅgha performed the act requiring amends, or another similar to it, or one worse than it; he does not disparage the act, he does not disparage those who performed it. Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with these five factors.”

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

“Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with eight factors. He does not suspend the Uposatha of a monk in good standing, he does not suspend the Pavāraṇā, he does not make himself difficult to speak to, he does not establish grounds for accusation, he does not make an opportunity, he does not accuse, he does not remind, and he does not associate with monks. Monks, the act requiring amends should be rescinded for a monk endowed with these eight factors.”

Paṭisāraṇīyakamme paṭippassambhetabbaaṭṭhārasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on the Eighteen to Be Rescinded Regarding the Act Requiring Amends is Concluded.

45. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena [tena hi (syā. ka.)], bhikkhave, sudhammena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

45.“And, monks, it should be rescinded in this way. Then, monks, the monk Sudhamma, having approached the Saṅgha, should arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior monks, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined palms, and say this: ‘Venerable sirs, having been subjected to the act requiring amends by the Saṅgha, I am conducting myself properly, I am showing humility, I am conducting myself in a way that leads to release. I request the rescission of the act requiring amends.’ He should request a second time. He should request a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma, against whom the Saṅgha has carried out the act requiring amends, is conducting himself properly, he is showing humility, he is conducting himself in a way that leads to release, and he requests the rescission of the act requiring amends. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, the Saṅgha may rescind the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma, against whom the Saṅgha has carried out the act requiring amends, is conducting himself properly, he is showing humility, he is conducting himself in a way that leads to release, and he requests the rescission of the act requiring amends. The Saṅgha rescinds the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma. If the rescission of the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma is agreeable to any venerable one, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.”

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ sudhammo bhikkhu saṅghena paṭisāraṇīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“For the second time, I speak on this matter… For the third time, I speak on this matter: Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This monk Sudhamma, against whom the Saṅgha has carried out the act requiring amends, is conducting himself properly, he is showing humility, he is conducting himself in a way that leads to release, and he requests the rescission of the act requiring amends. The Saṅgha rescinds the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma. If the rescission of the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma is agreeable to any venerable one, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.”

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena sudhammassa bhikkhuno paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

“The Saṅgha has rescinded the act requiring amends for the monk Sudhamma. It is agreeable to the Saṅgha, therefore it is silent. I shall bear it in mind thus.”

Paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ catutthaṃ.

The Fourth Act Requiring Amends is Concluded.

### 5. Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakammaṃ - The Act of Suspension for Not Seeing an Offense. ^5

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^5|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.5" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


46. Tena samayena buddho bhagavā kosambiyaṃ viharati ghositārāme. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā channo āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ passituṃ. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma āyasmā channo āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchissati āpattiṃ passitu’’nti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

46.At that time the Blessed One was dwelling at Kosambi, in Ghosita’s Park. Now at that time Venerable Channa had committed an offense but did not wish to see the offense. The monks who were modest … murmured, complained, and criticized him: “How can Venerable Channa, having committed an offense, not wish to see the offense?” Then those monks informed the Blessed One about this matter.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ passitu’’nti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ…pe… kathañhi nāma so, bhikkhave, moghapuriso āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchissati āpattiṃ passituṃ? Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karotu – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ – paṭhamaṃ channo bhikkhu codetabbo, codetvā sāretabbo, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbo, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and in this connection, had the Sangha of monks assembled and questioned the monks: “Is it true, monks, that the monk Channa has committed an offense and does not wish to see the offense?” “It is true, Blessed One.” The Blessed One rebuked him: “This is not fitting… … How can this foolish man, monks, commit an offense and not wish to see the offense? This will not lead to confidence in the unconvinced… … Having rebuked him … he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Well then, monks, let the Sangha carry out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha. And, monks, it should be done like this. First, the monk Channa should be questioned. Having been questioned, he should be reminded. Having been reminded, the offense should be imposed upon him. Having imposed the offense, a competent and capable monk should inform the Sangha:

47. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ passituṃ. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Esā ñatti.

47.‘Venerable sirs, let the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa has committed an offense and does not wish to see the offense. If it seems appropriate to the Sangha, the Sangha should carry out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha. This is the announcement.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ passituṃ. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“Venerable sirs, let the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa has committed an offense and does not wish to see the offense. The Sangha is carrying out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha. Any venerable one who approves of carrying out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha—should remain silent; any who disapproves should speak.”

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ passituṃ. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“For the second time I speak on this matter… For the third time I speak on this matter: Venerable sirs, let the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa has committed an offense and does not wish to see the offense. The Sangha is carrying out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha. Any venerable one who approves of carrying out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha—should remain silent; any who disapproves should speak.”

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmīti.

“The Sangha has carried out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not seeing the offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha. It is agreeable to the Sangha, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it in mind.”

‘‘Āvāsaparamparañca, bhikkhave, saṃsatha – ‘channo bhikkhu saṅghena āpattiyā [channo bhikkhu āpattiyā (sī. ka.)] adassane ukkhepanīyakammakato – asambhogaṃ saṅghenā’ti.

“And, monks, you should announce this in successive monasteries: ‘The monk Channa has been subjected to an act of suspension by the Sangha for not acknowledging an offense—non-intercourse with the Sangha.’”

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Group of Twelve Unrighteous Actions

48. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

48.“Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not acknowledging an offense, when endowed with three factors, is an unlawful act, a non-disciplinary act, and badly settled. It is done not in their presence, done without questioning, done without admission—endowed with these three factors, Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not acknowledging an offense is an unlawful act, a non-disciplinary act, and badly settled.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

“Furthermore, Bhikkhus, when endowed with another three factors, a suspension act for not acknowledging an offense is an unlawful act, a non-disciplinary act, and badly settled. It is done for a non-offense; done for an offense that does not require confession; done for an already confessed offense; done without charging; done without investigation; done without the offense being charged; done not in their presence; done unlawfully; done by a faction; done without questioning; done unlawfully; done by a faction; done without acknowledgment; done unlawfully; done by a faction; done for a non-offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction; done for an offense that does not require confession, done unlawfully, done by a faction; done for an already confessed offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction; done without charging, done unlawfully, done by a faction; done without investigation, done unlawfully, done by a faction; done without the offense being charged, done unlawfully, done by a faction—endowed with these three factors, Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not acknowledging an offense is an unlawful act, a non-disciplinary act, and badly settled.”

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The twelvefold unlawful procedure regarding suspension for not acknowledging an offense is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelvefold Lawful Act.

49. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

49.Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not admitting an offense, when endowed with three factors, is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well-appeased. It is done in the presence (of the Sangha), done with questioning, done upon acknowledgment—endowed with these three factors, Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not admitting an offense is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well-appeased.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ…pe…. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not admitting an offense, when endowed with three factors, is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well-appeased. (These are:) It is done concerning an offense; it is done concerning an offense requiring confession; it is done concerning an unconfessed offense. ... It is done after accusation; it is done after reminding; it is done after charging with an offense. ... It is done in the presence, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done by questioning, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done by admission, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done concerning an offense, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done concerning an offense requiring confession, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done concerning an unconfessed offense, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done after accusation, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done after reminding, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. ... It is done after charging with an offense, lawfully, and by a united Sangha. Endowed with these three factors, Bhikkhus, a suspension act for not admitting an offense is a lawful act, a disciplinary act, and well-appeased.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The twelvefold lawful act regarding the suspension for not admitting an offense is concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ

The Sixes on What is Wished For

50. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

50.Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities. He is quarrelsome, a maker of disputes, a maker of strife, a maker of wrangling, and a maker of legal issues in the Sangha; he is foolish, incompetent, frequently committing offenses, and unrepentant; he lives in association with householders, in unbecoming association with householders. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities. He is fallen away in higher virtue, fallen away in conduct, and fallen away in view. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities. He speaks in dispraise of the Buddha, speaks in dispraise of the Dhamma, and speaks in dispraise of the Sangha. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities.

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against three bhikkhus. One is a maker of quarrels, a maker of disputes, a maker of strife, a maker of wrangling, and a maker of legal issues in the Sangha; one is foolish, incompetent, frequently committing offenses, and unrepentant; one lives in association with householders, in unbecoming association with householders. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against these three bhikkhus.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against three further bhikkhus. One is fallen away in higher virtue, one is fallen away in conduct, and one is fallen away in view. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against these three bhikkhus.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Furthermore, monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against three further bhikkhus. One speaks in dispraise of the Buddha, one speaks in dispraise of the Dhamma, and one speaks in dispraise of the Sangha. Monks, the Sangha, if it wishes, may carry out an act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense against these three bhikkhus.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme

The Act of Suspension for Not Acknowledging an Offense

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Sixes on What is Wished For is concluded.

Tecattālīsavattaṃ

The forty-third section.

51. ‘‘Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāro, seyyābhihāro, pādodakaṃ, pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sāditabbaṃ. Na pakatatto bhikkhu sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na bhikkhu bhikkhūhi bhedetabbo [na bhikkhū bhikkhūhi bhedetabbā (syā.)], na gihiddhajo dhāretabbo, na titthiyaddhajo dhāretabbo, na titthiyā sevitabbā; bhikkhū sevitabbā, bhikkhusikkhāya sikkhitabbaṃ [bhikkhusikkhā sikkhitabbā (syā.)]. Na pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vatthabbaṃ, na ekacchanne anāvāse vatthabbaṃ, na ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vatthabbaṃ, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā vuṭṭhātabbaṃ, na pakatatto bhikkhu āsādetabbo anto vā bahi vā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

51.Bhikkhus, a bhikkhu who has been subjected to the act of suspension for not seeing an offense should behave properly. This is the proper conduct: He should not give ordination; he should not give dependence; he should not have a novice attend on him; he should not accept appointment as an instructor of nuns; even if appointed, he should not advise nuns. He should not commit the offense for which the Sangha has imposed the act of suspension for not seeing an offense, nor any similar offense, nor one more serious than that. He should not criticize the act, nor should he criticize those who performed the act. He should not accept from a regular bhikkhu salutation, rising up, the gesture of joined palms, or proper duties; nor the offering of a seat, the offering of a bed, water for the feet, a footstool, a foot wiper, the receiving of bowl and robe, or the massaging of the back while bathing. He should not disparage a regular bhikkhu for failure in virtue, for failure in conduct, for failure in view, or for failure in livelihood. He should not cause division among bhikkhus. He should not wear the banner of householders, nor should he wear the banner of other sects. He should not associate with other sectarians; he should associate with bhikkhus and train in the training of the bhikkhus. He should not dwell with a regular bhikkhu under the same roof in a lodging, nor under the same roof in an open space, nor under the same roof in a lodging or an open space. Seeing a regular bhikkhu, he should rise from his seat. He should not disparage a regular bhikkhu, whether inside or outside the monastery. He should not prevent a regular bhikkhu from observing the Uposatha, nor should he prevent him from performing the Pavāraṇā. He should not be given a formal caution, no accusation should be raised against him, no opportunity should be granted, he should not be admonished, he should not be reminded, nor should he associate with bhikkhus.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme

The act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense.

Tecattālīsavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The forty-third section is concluded.

52. Atha kho saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ akāsi – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. So saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato tamhā āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tattha bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garu kariṃsu [na garukariṃsu (ka.)], na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato tamhāpi āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tatthapi bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garuṃ kariṃsu, na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato tamhāpi āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tatthapi bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garuṃ kariṃsu, na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato punadeva kosambiṃ paccāgañchi. So sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘ahaṃ, āvuso, saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe…. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

52.Then the Sangha performed the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not acknowledging his offense—he was to have no association with the Sangha. Having been subjected to the act of suspension by the Sangha for not acknowledging his offense, he left that monastery and went to another. There the bhikkhus neither greeted him, nor rose up for him, nor offered a gesture of reverence, nor proper service; they did not honor, respect, esteem, or venerate him. Being thus dishonored, disrespected, unesteemed, and unvenerated by the bhikkhus, and treated with disrespect, he left that monastery too and went to another. There too the bhikkhus neither greeted him, nor rose up for him, nor offered a gesture of reverence, nor proper service; they did not honor, respect, esteem, or venerate him. Being thus dishonored, disrespected, unesteemed, and unvenerated by the bhikkhus, and treated with disrespect, he left that monastery too and went to another. There too the bhikkhus neither greeted him, nor rose up for him, nor offered a gesture of reverence, nor proper service; they did not honor, respect, esteem, or venerate him. Being thus dishonored, disrespected, unesteemed, and unvenerated by the bhikkhus, and treated with disrespect, he eventually returned to Kosambi. He behaved properly, made himself amenable, conducted himself correctly, and approached the bhikkhus, saying: "Venerables, I have been subjected to the act of suspension by the Sangha for not acknowledging my offense. I now behave properly, make myself amenable, and conduct myself correctly. What should I do next?" The bhikkhus reported this matter to the Blessed One… "Well then, bhikkhus, let the Sangha rescind the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not acknowledging his offense."

Nappaṭippassambhetabba-tecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-Three Not to Be Revoked

53. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

53.Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He ordains, gives dependence, has a novice attend on him, accepts the appointment as an instructor of bhikkhus, and even when appointed, instructs bhikkhunīs. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He commits the offense for which the Saṅgha had imposed the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense, or another offense similar to it, or one even worse than it; he criticizes the act, he criticizes those who performed the act. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāraṃ sādiyati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He accepts the acts of reverence, rising to greet, raising joined palms, proper etiquette, and offering a seat from a bhikkhu in good standing. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno seyyābhihāraṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ, pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sādiyati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He accepts the offering of a bed, foot-washing water, a footstool, a foot-scraper, the receiving of his bowl and robes, and back-rubbing during bathing from a bhikkhu in good standing. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, bhikkhuṃ [bhikkhū (sī. syā.)] bhikkhūhi bhedeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He denounces a bhikkhu in good standing for failing in virtue, he denounces a bhikkhu in good standing for failing in conduct, he denounces a bhikkhu in good standing for failing in view, he denounces a bhikkhu in good standing for failing in livelihood, and he causes division among the bhikkhus. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Gihiddhajaṃ dhāreti, titthiyaddhajaṃ dhāreti, titthiye sevati; bhikkhū na sevati, bhikkhusikkhāya na sikkhati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He bears the insignia of a householder, he bears the insignia of a sectarian, he associates with sectarians; he does not associate with bhikkhus, he does not train in the training of bhikkhus. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vasati, ekacchanne anāvāse vasati, ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vasati; pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā na vuṭṭhāti; pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ āsādeti anto vā bahi vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a bhikkhu endowed with five other qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He lives with a bhikkhu in good standing in the same covered dwelling; he lives with a bhikkhu in good standing in the same uncovered dwelling; he lives with a bhikkhu in good standing in the same covered or uncovered dwelling. Upon seeing a bhikkhu in good standing, he does not rise from his seat. He harasses a bhikkhu in good standing, whether inside or outside. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these five qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with eight qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked. He prevents a bhikkhu in good standing from observing the Uposatha, he prevents the Pavāraṇā, he makes himself amenable to admonition, he establishes a ground for accusation, he asks for an opportunity (to speak), he charges, he reminds, he associates with bhikkhus. Monks, a bhikkhu endowed with these eight qualities should not have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense revoked.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme

The Act of Suspension for Not Acknowledging an Offense

Nappaṭippassambhetabba-tecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-Three Not to Be Revoked is completed.

Paṭippassambhetabba-tecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-three to be Rescinded

54. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

54.Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not give ordination, he does not give dependence, he does not have a novice attend on him, he does not approve the agreement to be a monk's instructor for nuns, and even if agreed to, he does not instruct the nuns—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not commit the offense for which the Sangha imposed the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense, nor one similar to it, nor one worse than it; he does not disparage the act, nor those who performed the act—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāraṃ sādiyati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not approve of being greeted respectfully, being stood up for, being saluted with joined palms, proper service, or an offering of a seat from a monk in good standing—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno seyyābhihāraṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ, pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sādiyati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not approve of a monk in good standing's offering of a bed, foot-washing water, a footstool, a foot-wiping cloth, or the receiving of bowl and robe, nor back-rubbing in the bath—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na bhikkhuṃ bhikkhūhi bhedeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not denounce a monk in good standing for failure in virtue, failure in conduct, failure in view, failure in livelihood, nor does he cause division among the monks—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na gihiddhajaṃ dhāreti, na titthiyaddhajaṃ dhāreti, na titthiye sevati, bhikkhū sevati, bhikkhusikkhāya sikkhati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not wear the emblem of a householder, nor the emblem of a sectarian, he does not associate with sectarians, he associates with monks, and he trains in the training of the monks—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vasati, na ekacchanne anāvāse vasati, na ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vasati, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā vuṭṭhāti, na pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ āsādeti anto vā bahi vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not dwell in the same dwelling with a monk in good standing, he does not dwell in the same open space with a monk in good standing, he does not dwell in the same dwelling or open space with a monk in good standing, he rises from his seat upon seeing a monk in good standing, he does not approach a monk in good standing inside or outside—a monk endowed with these five qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, a monk endowed with eight qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded. He does not prevent a monk in good standing from observing the Uposatha, he does not prevent him from performing the Pavāraṇā, he does not make him subject to formal censure, he does not initiate an accusation, he does not request an opportunity, he does not rebuke, he does not remind, and he does not associate him with other monks—a monk endowed with these eight qualities should have the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense rescinded.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakamme

The Act of Suspension for Not Acknowledging an Offense

Paṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-three to be Rescinded is completed.

55. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena, bhikkhave, channena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

55.And, monks, this is how it should be rescinded. That monk Channa, having approached the Sangha, should arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior monks, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined hands, and say this: ‘Venerable sirs, I have been rightfully subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense. I am behaving properly, I am shaving my hair, I am seeking rehabilitation, and I request the rescinding of the act of suspension for not acknowledging the offense.’ He should be asked a second time. He should be asked a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Sangha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa, having been subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense, is conducting himself properly: he is shaving his hair, he is seeking rehabilitation, and he requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense. If it is agreeable to the Sangha, the Sangha may rescind the act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa, having been subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense, is conducting himself properly: he is shaving his hair, he is seeking rehabilitation, and he requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense. The Sangha rescinds the act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense. Whichever venerable one approves of the rescinding of the act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense, let him be silent; whichever does not approve, let him speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

I speak on this matter a second time... I speak on this matter a third time: Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk Channa, having been subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense, is conducting himself properly: he is shaving his hair, he is seeking rehabilitation, and he requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense. The Sangha rescinds the act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense. Whichever venerable one approves of the rescinding of the act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense, let him be silent; whichever does not approve, let him speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The act of suspension for the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense has been rescinded by the Sangha. The Sangha approves, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

Āpattiyā adassane ukkhepanīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ pañcamaṃ.

The fifth act of suspension for not acknowledging an offense is concluded.

### 6. Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakammaṃ - The act of suspension for not making amends for an offense. ^6

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^6|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.6" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


56. Tena samayena buddho bhagavā kosambiyaṃ viharati ghositārāme. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā channo āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ paṭikātuṃ. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma āyasmā channo āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchissati āpattiṃ paṭikātu’’nti? Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

56.At that time the Blessed One was dwelling at Kosambi in Ghosita's Park. Now at that time Venerable Channa had committed an offense but was unwilling to make amends for it. Those monks who were modest… grumbled, criticized, and spread it about: “How could Venerable Channa commit an offense and then be unwilling to make amends for it?” Then those monks reported the matter to the Blessed One.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ paṭikātu’’nti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ…pe… kathañhi nāma so, bhikkhave, moghapuriso āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchissati āpattiṃ paṭikātuṃ. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karotu – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, kātabbaṃ – paṭhamaṃ channo bhikkhu codetabbo, codetvā sāretabbo, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbo, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, because of this matter, having convened the Sangha of monks, questioned the monks: "Is it true, monks, that the monk Channa, having committed an offense, does not wish to make amends for the offense?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Blessed One rebuked him: "It is unsuitable... How could that foolish man, monks, having committed an offense, not wish to make amends for the offense? This will not lead to confidence in the unconvinced... Having rebuked him... having given a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: "Therefore, monks, let the Sangha carry out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha. And this, monks, is how it should be done: First, the monk Channa should be questioned, then reminded, then the offense should be brought to his attention, and having brought the offense to his attention, a monk who is articulate and competent should inform the Sangha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ paṭikātuṃ. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Esā ñatti.

"Listen to me, venerable Sangha. This monk Channa, having committed an offense, does not wish to make amends for the offense. If the Sangha is ready, let the Sangha carry out the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ paṭikātuṃ. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Listen to me, venerable Sangha. This monk Channa, having committed an offense, does not wish to make amends for the offense. The Sangha performs the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha. If this is agreeable to the venerable ones, that the Sangha should perform the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha, let them remain silent. If anyone does not approve, let him speak."

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu āpattiṃ āpajjitvā na icchati āpattiṃ paṭikātuṃ. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"I speak on this matter a second time... I speak on this matter a third time—venerable Sangha, listen to me. This monk Channa, having committed an offense, does not wish to make amends for the offense. The Sangha performs the act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha. If this act of suspension against the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—non-association with the Sangha—is agreeable to any venerable one, let him remain silent. If it is not agreeable to anyone, let him speak."

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmīti.

"The Sangha has performed the act of suspension against the monk Channa for his failure to make amends for his offense—excluding him from association with the Sangha. The Sangha approves; therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it."

‘‘Āvāsaparamparañca, bhikkhave, saṃsatha – ‘channo bhikkhu, saṅghena āpattiyā [channo bhikkhu āpattiyā (sī. ka.)] appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato – asambhogaṃ saṅghenā’ti.

"Furthermore, monks, you should announce this from residence to residence: ‘The monk Channa, because he has not made amends for his offense, has been subjected to an act of suspension by the Sangha—excluding him from association with the Sangha.’"

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Section on Twelve Unlawful Acts

57. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

57.Monks, an act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, endowed with three factors, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled. It is done in absence, done without questioning, done without admission. Endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension for not making amends for an offense is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

Furthermore, monks, an act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, endowed with these three factors, is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled. It is done for a non-offense; it is done for an offense not requiring confession; it is done for an offense that has been confessed... it is done without accusation; it is done without investigation; it is done without charging with an offense... it is done in absence, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done without questioning, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done without admission, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done for a non-offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done for an offense not requiring confession, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done for an offense that has been confessed, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done without accusation, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done without investigation, done unlawfully, done by a faction... it is done without charging with an offense, done unlawfully, done by a faction. Endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension for not making amends for an offense is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

Act of Suspension for Failure to Make Amends for an Offense

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on Twelve Unlawful Acts is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelve Legitimate Acts

58. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

58.“Monks, an act of suspension for not abandoning an offense, when endowed with three factors, is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and is well-settled. It is done in the presence, it is done after questioning, it is done after acknowledgment—endowed with these three factors, monks, an act of suspension for not abandoning an offense is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and is well-settled.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

“Furthermore, monks, an act of suspension for not abandoning an offense, when endowed with three factors, is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and is well-settled.
