It is done regarding an offense; it is done regarding an offense that leads to confession; it is done regarding an offense that has not been confessed… It is done after accusation; it is done after reminding; it is done after charging with an offense… It is done in the presence, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done after questioning, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done after acknowledgment, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done regarding an offense, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done regarding an offense that leads to confession, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done regarding an offense that has not been confessed, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done after accusation, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done after reminding, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha… It is done after charging with an offense, it is done according to the Dhamma, it is done by a united Saṅgha. Monks, an act of suspension for not abandoning an offense, when endowed with these three factors, is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and is well-settled.”

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

Act of Suspension for Not Abandoning an Offense

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Twelve Legitimate Acts are concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ

The Six Things Wished For

59. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

59.Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three factors. He is a maker of quarrels, a maker of disputes, a maker of arguments, a maker of noise, and a maker of legal issues in the Saṅgha; he is foolish, incompetent, frequently committing offenses, and does not offer a way out; he lives in improper association with householders. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three factors.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three factors. He is fallen away from higher virtue, fallen away from conduct, and fallen away from view. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three factors.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with three factors. He speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, and speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against a bhikkhu endowed with these three factors.

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against three bhikkhus. One is a maker of quarrels, a maker of disputes, a maker of arguments, a maker of noise, and a maker of legal issues in the Saṅgha; one is foolish, incompetent, frequently committing offenses, and does not offer a way out; one lives in improper association with householders. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against these three bhikkhus.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against three bhikkhus. One is fallen away from higher virtue, one is fallen away from conduct, and one is fallen away from view. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against these three bhikkhus.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against three bhikkhus. One speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, one speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, and one speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. If the Saṅgha wishes, it may carry out an act of suspension for an unrectified offense against these three bhikkhus.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

Act of Suspension for an Unrectified Offense

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Six Things Wished For Concluded.

Tecattālīsavattaṃ

The forty-third section.

60. ‘‘Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāro, seyyābhihāro, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ, pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sāditabbaṃ. Na pakatatto bhikkhu sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃsetabbo, na bhikkhu bhikkhūhi bhedetabbo. Na gihiddhajo dhāretabbo, na titthiyaddhajo dhāretabbo, na titthiyā sevitabbā; bhikkhū sevitabbā, bhikkhusikkhāya sikkhitabbaṃ. Na pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vatthabbaṃ, na ekacchanne anāvāse vatthabbaṃ, na ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vatthabbaṃ, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā vuṭṭhātabbaṃ, na pakatatto bhikkhu āsādetabbo anto vā bahi vā. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

60.A monk on whom the Sangha has imposed the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, bhikkhus, should behave properly. Herein is the proper conduct: He should not give ordination, he should not give dependence, he should not have a novice attend on him, he should not accept appointment as an advisor of nuns, and even if appointed, he should not advise nuns. He should not commit the offense for which the Sangha imposed the act of suspension for not making amends, nor one similar, nor one worse. He should not criticize the act, nor those who performed it. He should not accept from a regular monk salutation, rising, the gesture of joined palms, proper duties, the offering of a seat, the offering of a bed, water for washing the feet, a footstool, a foot scraper, the receiving of his bowl and robe, or back-rubbing during a bath. He should not denounce a regular monk for failure in virtue, failure in conduct, failure in view, or failure in livelihood. He should not cause division among the monks. He should not carry a layman’s banner, nor a sectarian banner, nor associate with sectarians; he should associate with monks and train in the training of the monks. He should not dwell with a regular monk under the same roof in a dwelling, nor in a non-dwelling, nor in a dwelling or non-dwelling. Upon seeing a regular monk, he should rise from his seat. A regular monk should not be disparaged by him, whether inside or outside. He should not prevent a regular monk from observing the Uposatha, nor from performing the Pavāraṇā, nor should he give instructions, nor lay down a censure, nor demand an admission of the offense, nor accuse, nor remind, nor should he associate with the monks.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

Act of Suspension for Failure to Make Amends for an Offense

Tecattālīsavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The forty-third section is concluded.

61. Atha kho saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ akāsi – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. So saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato tamhā āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tattha bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garuṃ kariṃsu, na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato tamhāpi āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tatthapi bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garuṃ kariṃsu, na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato tamhāpi āvāsā aññaṃ āvāsaṃ agamāsi. Tatthapi bhikkhū neva abhivādesuṃ, na paccuṭṭhesuṃ, na añjalikammaṃ na sāmīcikammaṃ akaṃsu, na sakkariṃsu, na garuṃ kariṃsu, na mānesuṃ, na pūjesuṃ. So bhikkhūhi asakkariyamāno agarukariyamāno amāniyamāno apūjiyamāno asakkārapakato punadeva kosambiṃ paccāgañchi. So sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘ahaṃ, āvuso, saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe…. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

61.Then the Sangha imposed the act of suspension on the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense—namely, non-association with the Sangha. Having been suspended by the Sangha for not making amends for his offense, he left that monastery and went to another monastery. There the monks neither greeted him, nor rose for him, nor offered the gesture of joined palms, nor performed proper duties, nor honored him, nor respected him, nor esteemed him, nor venerated him. Not being honored, respected, esteemed, or venerated by the monks, being deprived of respect, he left that monastery too and went to another monastery. There also the monks neither greeted him, nor rose for him, nor offered the gesture of joined palms, nor performed proper duties, nor honored him, nor respected him, nor esteemed him, nor venerated him. Not being honored, respected, esteemed, or venerated by the monks, being deprived of respect, he left that monastery too and went to another monastery. There also the monks neither greeted him, nor rose for him, nor offered the gesture of joined palms, nor performed proper duties, nor honored him, nor respected him, nor esteemed him, nor venerated him. Not being honored, respected, esteemed, or venerated by the monks, being deprived of respect, he returned once more to Kosambi. He behaved properly, shaved his hair, sought rehabilitation, and approaching the monks, he said: "Friends, having been suspended by the Sangha for not making amends for my offense, I now behave properly, shave my hair, and seek rehabilitation. What should I do now?" The monks reported this matter to the Blessed One… "Well then, bhikkhus, let the Sangha rescind the act of suspension on the monk Channa for not making amends for his offense."

Nappaṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-Third: On Not Revoking

62. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

62.Monks, a monk endowed with five factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked. He confers ordination, he gives dependence, he has a novice attend on him, he assents to the appointment as an instructor of nuns, and even though appointed, he instructs nuns. A monk endowed with these five factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked.

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati…pe… pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāraṃ sādiyati…pe… pakatattassa bhikkhuno seyyābhihāraṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ, pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sādiyati…pe… pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, bhikkhuṃ bhikkhūhi bhedeti…pe… gihiddhajaṃ dhāreti, titthiyaddhajaṃ dhāreti, titthiye sevati, bhikkhū na sevati, bhikkhusikkhāya na sikkhati…pe… pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vasati, ekacchanne anāvāse vasati, ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vasati, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā na vuṭṭhāti, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ āsādeti anto vā bahi vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with five factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked. He commits the offense for which the Sangha imposed the act of suspension when there was no making amends for the offense, or one similar to it, or even worse than it; he disparages the act, he disparages those who performed the act… He approves of bowing down to, standing up for, reverential salutation, proper duties, or the offering of a seat to a regular monk… He approves of the offering of a bed, foot-water, a footstool, a foot-wiping cloth, or receiving a bowl and robe, or having his back rubbed while bathing, from a regular monk… He denounces a regular monk for failure in virtue, failure in conduct, failure in view, or failure in livelihood; he causes division among the monks… He wears the emblem of a householder, the emblem of a sectarian; he associates with sectarians and does not associate with monks; he does not train in the training of the monks… He dwells under the same roof with a regular monk, in the same non-monastic dwelling, or in the same dwelling, whether monastic or non-monastic; when seeing a regular monk, he does not rise from his seat; he harasses a regular monk, whether inside or outside. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Monks, a monk endowed with eight factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked. He obstructs a monk in good standing from observing the Uposatha, he obstructs the Pavāraṇā, he makes himself liable to admonition, he sets up a charge, he causes an opportunity (for accusation), he accuses, he reminds, he causes monks to be involved. Monks, a monk endowed with these eight factors—when there is no making amends for an offense—should not have the act of suspension revoked.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

The Act of Suspension for Failure to Make Amends for an Offense

Nappaṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-Third on Not Revoking is completed.

Paṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-three on What Should Be Rescinded.

63. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

63.Bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded. He does not give higher ordination; he does not give dependence; he does not have a novice attend upon him; he does not accept the appointment to advise bhikkhunīs, nor, even if appointed, does he advise bhikkhunīs. Bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati…pe… na pakatattassa bhikkhuno abhivādanaṃ, paccuṭṭhānaṃ, añjalikammaṃ, sāmīcikammaṃ, āsanābhihāraṃ sādiyati…pe… na pakatattassa bhikkhuno seyyābhihāraṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ, pādakathalikaṃ, pattacīvarappaṭiggahaṇaṃ, nahāne piṭṭhiparikammaṃ sādiyati…pe… na pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ sīlavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na ācāravipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na diṭṭhivipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na ājīvavipattiyā anuddhaṃseti, na bhikkhuṃ bhikkhūhi bhedeti…pe… na gihiddhajaṃ dhāreti, na titthiyaddhajaṃ dhāreti, na titthiye sevati, bhikkhū sevati, bhikkhusikkhāya sikkhati…pe… na pakatattena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ ekacchanne āvāse vasati, na ekacchanne anāvāse vasati, na ekacchanne āvāse vā anāvāse vā vasati, pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ disvā āsanā vuṭṭhāti, na pakatattaṃ bhikkhuṃ āsādeti anto vā bahi vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Again, bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded. He does not commit the offense for which the Sangha imposed the act of suspension for not making amends, nor another offense of a similar kind, nor one more serious than that; he does not disparage the act, nor those who performed it… He does not accept the bowing down to, rising up for, saluting with joined palms, proper duties, or the offering of a seat from a bhikkhu in good standing… He does not accept the offering of a bed, foot-water, a footstool, a foot-wiping cloth, the receiving of bowl and robe, or back-rubbing while bathing from a bhikkhu in good standing… He does not reproach a bhikkhu in good standing for failure in virtue, failure in conduct, failure in view, or failure in livelihood; he does not cause a schism among bhikkhus… He does not bear the banner of householders, nor the banner of sectarians; he does not associate with sectarians, but associates with bhikkhus and trains in the training of bhikkhus… He does not dwell under the same roof with a bhikkhu in good standing, whether in a monastery or outside a monastery; upon seeing a bhikkhu in good standing, he rises from his seat; he does not harass a bhikkhu in good standing, whether inside or outside. Bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

Bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with eight factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded. He does not suspend the Uposatha of a bhikkhu in good standing; he does not suspend the Pavāraṇā; he does not make himself amenable to instruction; he does not initiate a charge; he does not ask for an opportunity; he does not admonish; he does not remind; he does not associate with bhikkhus. Bhikkhus, the act of suspension against a bhikkhu endowed with these eight factors, for not making amends for an offense, should be rescinded.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakamme

Act of Suspension for Failure to Make Amends for an Offense

Paṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-three on What Should Be Rescinded is Completed.

64. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena bhikkhave, channena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

64.And, bhikkhus, it should be rescinded in this way. Then that bhikkhu Channa, having approached the Sangha, should arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior bhikkhus, sit in a squatting position, raising his hands in añjali, and say this: ‘Venerable Sirs, I, having been subjected to the act of suspension by the Sangha for not making amends for an offense, am conducting myself correctly, I am letting my hair grow, I am conducting myself so as to be restored, and I request the rescinding of the act of suspension for not making amends for the offense.’ He should be requested a second time, and a third time. A competent and capable bhikkhu should then inform the Sangha thus:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable Sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This bhikkhu Channa, against whom the Sangha has imposed the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, is conducting himself correctly, letting his hair grow, conducting himself so as to be restored, and requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense. If it is appropriate for the Sangha, the Sangha may rescind the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable Sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This bhikkhu Channa, against whom the Sangha has imposed the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, is conducting himself correctly, letting his hair grow, conducting himself so as to be restored, and requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense. The Sangha rescinds the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense. Any venerable one who approves of the rescinding of the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense should remain silent; whoever does not approve should speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ channo bhikkhu saṅghena, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For a second time I speak on this matter… For a third time I speak on this matter: Venerable Sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This bhikkhu Channa, against whom the Sangha has imposed the act of suspension for not making amends for an offense, is conducting himself correctly, letting his hair grow, conducting himself so as to be restored, and requests the rescinding of the act of suspension for not making amends for the offense. The Sangha rescinds the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense. Any venerable one who approves of the rescinding of the act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense should remain silent; whoever does not approve should speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena channassa bhikkhuno, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The act of suspension against the bhikkhu Channa for not making amends for an offense has been rescinded by the Sangha. The Sangha approves of it, and is therefore silent. Thus I hold it.

Āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhepanīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ chaṭṭhaṃ.

The Act of Suspension for Failure to Make Amends for an Offense is Concluded, the Sixth.

### 7. Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakammaṃ - The Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing an Evil View ^7

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv11-brahmali-pali#^7|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV11.7" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


65. [idaṃ vatthu pāci. 417; ma. ni. 234 ādayo] Tena samayena buddho bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena ariṭṭhassa nāma bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa [gandhabādhipubbassa (ka.)] evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ hoti – ‘‘tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti. Assosuṃ kho sambahulā bhikkhū ariṭṭhassa nāma kira bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – ‘‘tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū yena ariṭṭho bhikkhu gaddhabādhipubbo tenupasaṅkamiṃsu. Upasaṅkamitvā ariṭṭhaṃ bhikkhuṃ gaddhabādhipubbaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘saccaṃ kira te, āvuso ariṭṭha, evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti? ‘‘Evaṃbyā kho ahaṃ, āvuso, bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi, yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti.

65.At one time the Blessed One was dwelling at Sāvatthī, in Jeta’s Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika’s Park. Now at that time a monk named Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, had conceived such an evil view: ‘As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’ A number of monks heard that the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, had conceived such an evil view: ‘As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’ Then those monks approached the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer. Having approached, they said to the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer: ‘Is it true, friend Ariṭṭha, that you have conceived such an evil view: “As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them”?’ ‘Just so, friends. As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’

‘‘Māvuso ariṭṭha, evaṃ avaca. Mā bhagavantaṃ abbhācikkhi. Na hi sādhu bhagavato abbhakkhānaṃ [abbhācikkhanaṃ (ka.)]. Na hi bhagavā evaṃ vadeyya. Anekapariyāyenāvuso ariṭṭha, antarāyikā dhammā antarāyikā vuttā bhagavatā. Alañca pana te paṭisevato antarāyāya. Appassādā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā, bahudukkhā bahupāyāsā [bahūpāyāsā (sī. syā.)], ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo. Aṭṭhikaṅkalūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā, bahudukkhā bahūpāyāsā, ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo. Maṃsapesūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā…pe… tiṇukkūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā…pe… aṅgārakāsūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… supinakūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… yācitakūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… rukkhaphalūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… asisūnūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… sattisūlūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā… sappasirūpamā kāmā vuttā bhagavatā, bahudukkhā bahūpāyāsā, ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo’’ti.

“Do not speak thus, friend Ariṭṭha. Do not misrepresent the Blessed One. It is not good to misrepresent the Blessed One. The Blessed One would not speak thus. In many ways, friend Ariṭṭha, the Blessed One has declared things that are impediments to be impediments. And they are indeed sufficient to be an impediment for one who engages in them. Sensual pleasures have been declared by the Blessed One to have little satisfaction, to be full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater. Sensual pleasures have been declared by the Blessed One to be like a skeleton, full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater. Sensual pleasures have been declared by the Blessed One to be like a lump of flesh… like a grass torch… like a pit of glowing embers… like a dream… like borrowed goods… like fruit on a tree… like a butcher’s knife… like a spear-point… like a snake’s head—full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater.”

Evampi kho ariṭṭho bhikkhu gaddhabādhipubbo tehi bhikkhūhi vuccamāno tatheva taṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ thāmasā parāmāsā abhinivissa voharati – ‘‘evaṃbyā kho ahaṃ, āvuso, bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi, yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti. Yato ca kho te bhikkhū nāsakkhiṃsu ariṭṭhaṃ bhikkhuṃ gaddhabādhipubbaṃ etasmā pāpakā diṭṭhigatā vivecetuṃ, atha kho te bhikkhū yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā ariṭṭhaṃ bhikkhuṃ gaddhabādhipubbaṃ paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira te, ariṭṭha, evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti? ‘‘Evaṃbyā kho ahaṃ, bhante, bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi, yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyā’’ti.

Even though the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, was spoken to by those monks in this way, he still clung firmly to that evil view and persisted in declaring: ‘Just so, friends. As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’ And when those monks were unable to dissuade the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, from that evil view, they approached the Blessed One. Having approached, they reported the matter to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and for this reason, had the Saṅgha of bhikkhus assembled and questioned the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer: ‘Is it true, Ariṭṭha, that such an evil view has arisen in you—that you understand the Dhamma taught by me in such a way that those things declared by me to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them?’ ‘Just so, Venerable sir. As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’

‘‘Kassa nu kho nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, mayā evaṃ dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāsi? Nanu mayā, moghapurisa, anekapariyāyena antarāyikā dhammā antarāyikā vuttā? Alañca pana te paṭisevato antarāyāya. Appassādā kāmā vuttā mayā, bahudukkhā bahupāyāsā, ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo. Aṭṭhikaṅkalūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā, bahudukkhā bahupāyāsā, ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo. Maṃsapesūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā…pe… tiṇukkūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… aṅgārakāsūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… supinakūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā…pe… yācitakūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… rukkhaphalūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… asisūnūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… sattisūlūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā… sappasirūpamā kāmā vuttā mayā, bahudukkhā bahupāyāsā, ādīnavo ettha bhiyyo. Atha ca pana tvaṃ, moghapurisa, attanā duggahitena [duggahitena diṭṭhigatena (syā.)] amhe ceva abbhācikkhasi, attānañca khaṇasi, bahuñca apuññaṃ pasavasi. Tañhi te, moghapurisa, bhavissati dīgharattaṃ ahitāya dukkhāya. Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karotu – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Evañca pana bhikkhave kātabbaṃ – paṭhamaṃ ariṭṭho bhikkhu codetabbo, codetvā sāretabbo, sāretvā āpattiṃ āropetabbo, āpattiṃ āropetvā byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

“Foolish man, in whose name do you claim to understand the Dhamma taught by me in this way? Foolish man, have I not in many ways declared things that are impediments to be impediments? And they are indeed sufficient to be an impediment for one who engages in them. I have declared sensual pleasures to be of little satisfaction, to be full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater. I have declared sensual pleasures to be like a skeleton, full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater. I have declared sensual pleasures to be like a lump of flesh… like a grass torch… like a pit of glowing embers… like a dream… like borrowed goods… like fruit on a tree… like a butcher’s knife… like a spear-point… like a snake’s head—full of suffering, full of vexation, and the danger in them is greater. Yet you, foolish man, by your wrong grasp, not only misrepresent us but also harm yourself and produce much demerit. This, foolish man, will lead to your long-term harm and suffering. This, foolish man, does not lead to the confidence of those without faith, nor to the increase of confidence in those with faith.” Having rebuked him… and given a Dhamma talk, he addressed the bhikkhus: “Well then, bhikkhus, let the Saṅgha perform the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha. And this, bhikkhus, is how it should be done: First, the monk Ariṭṭha should be charged. Having been charged, he should be reminded. Having been reminded, the offense should be imposed. Having imposed the offense, a competent and capable bhikkhu should inform the Saṅgha—”

66. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyāti. So taṃ diṭṭhiṃ na paṭinissajjati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Esā ñatti.

66.“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. The monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, has conceived such an evil view: ‘As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’ He does not relinquish that view. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, let the Saṅgha perform the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha. This is the motion.”

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyāti. So taṃ diṭṭhiṃ na paṭinissajjati. Saṅgho ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. The monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, has conceived such an evil view: ‘As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.’ He does not relinquish that view. The Saṅgha performs the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha. Any venerable one who approves of the performance of the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha—should remain silent. Any who does not approve should speak up.”

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa evarūpaṃ pāpakaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ – tathāhaṃ bhagavatā dhammaṃ desitaṃ ājānāmi yathā yeme antarāyikā dhammā vuttā bhagavatā te paṭisevato nālaṃ antarāyāyāti. So taṃ diṭṭhiṃ na paṭinissajjati. Saṅgho ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ karoti – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Yassāyasmato khamati ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa karaṇaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“For a second time I speak on this matter… For a third time I speak on this matter: ‘Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. The monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, has conceived such an evil view: “As I understand the Dhamma taught by the Blessed One, those things declared by the Blessed One to be impediments are not in fact impediments for one who engages in them.” He does not relinquish that view. The Saṅgha performs the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha. Any venerable one who approves of the performance of the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha—should remain silent. Any who does not approve should speak up.’

‘‘Kataṃ saṅghena ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmīti.

The Saṅgha has performed the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha. The Saṅgha approves of it, therefore it is silent. Thus do I hold it.”

‘‘Āvāsaparamparañca, bhikkhave, saṃsatha – ‘ariṭṭho bhikkhu gaddhabādhipubbo, saṅghena pāpikāya [gaddhabādhipubbo pāpikāya (sī. ka.)] diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato – asambhogaṃ saṅghenā’’’ti.

“And, bhikkhus, announce this from residence to residence: ‘The monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture-trainer, has been subjected to the act of suspension by the Saṅgha for not relinquishing his evil view—non-association with the Saṅgha.’ ”

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelvefold Unlawful Act

67. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Asammukhā kataṃ hoti, appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

67."Monks, a suspension act for not relinquishing an evil view is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled when it is endowed with three factors: it is done in the absence (of the accused); it is done without questioning; it is done without admission. Monks, a suspension act for not relinquishing an evil view is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled when it is endowed with these three factors."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca. Anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, asāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… asammukhā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… appaṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… anāpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… acodetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… asāretvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ anāropetvā kataṃ hoti, adhammena kataṃ hoti, vaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ adhammakammañca hoti, avinayakammañca, duvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, a suspension act for not relinquishing an evil view is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled when it is endowed with three factors. It is done: when there is no offense, unlawfully, by a faction; for an offense that does not lead to confession, unlawfully, by a faction; for an offense that has been confessed, unlawfully, by a faction; without accusation, unlawfully, by a faction; without inquiry, unlawfully, by a faction; without stating the offense, unlawfully, by a faction; not in the presence, unlawfully, by a faction; without questioning, unlawfully, by a faction; without admission, unlawfully, by a faction. Monks, a suspension act for not relinquishing an evil view is an unlawful act, contrary to the Discipline, and improperly settled when it is endowed with these three factors."

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakamme

Concerning the Suspension Act for Not Relinquishing an Evil View

Adhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Twelvefold Unlawful Act is concluded.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ

The Twelvefold Legitimate Act.

68. ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Sammukhā kataṃ hoti, paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

68."Monks, when an act of suspension for not relinquishing a bad view is endowed with three factors, it is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and well-settled. It is done face to face, done after questioning, and done after admission. Monks, when an act of suspension for not relinquishing a bad view is endowed with these three factors, it is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and well-settled."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca. Āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, sāretvā kataṃ hoti, āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti…pe… sammukhā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭipucchā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… paṭiññāya kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… desanāgāminiyā āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… adesitāya āpattiyā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… codetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… sāretvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti…pe… āpattiṃ āropetvā kataṃ hoti, dhammena kataṃ hoti, samaggena kataṃ hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgataṃ, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ dhammakammañca hoti, vinayakammañca, suvūpasantañca.

"Furthermore, monks, when an act of suspension for not relinquishing a bad view is endowed with three factors, it is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and well-settled. It is done for an offense, done for an offense requiring confession, done for an unconfessed offense. It is done after accusing, done after reminding, done after imputing an offense. It is done face-to-face, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done after questioning, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done upon acknowledgment, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done for an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done for an offense requiring confession, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done for an unconfessed offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done after accusing, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done after reminding, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. It is done after imputing an offense, done in accordance with the Dhamma, done by a united Sangha. Monks, when an act of suspension for not relinquishing a bad view is endowed with these three factors, it is a legitimate act, a Vinaya act, and well-settled."

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakamme

Regarding the Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing a Bad View.

Dhammakammadvādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Twelve Legitimate Disciplinary Acts are Concluded.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ

The Sixes on Aspirations

69. [pari. 323] ‘‘Tīhi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

69.Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with three qualities for not relinquishing a bad view. He is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, verbose, and creates legal issues in the Saṅgha; he is foolish, incompetent, commits many offenses, and is not apologetic; he lives in association with householders, in inappropriate association with householders. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities for not relinquishing a bad view.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with three further qualities for not relinquishing a bad view. He is deficient in higher virtue, deficient in conduct, and deficient in view. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities for not relinquishing a bad view.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, tīhaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with three further qualities for not relinquishing a bad view. He speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on a bhikkhu endowed with these three qualities for not relinquishing a bad view.

‘‘Tiṇṇaṃ, bhikkhave, bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko bhaṇḍanakārako hoti kalahakārako vivādakārako bhassakārako saṅghe adhikaraṇakārako; eko bālo hoti abyatto āpattibahulo anapadāno; eko gihisaṃsaṭṭho viharati ananulomikehi gihisaṃsaggehi – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view. One is quarrelsome, contentious, disputatious, verbose, and creates legal issues in the Saṅgha; one is foolish, incompetent, commits many offenses, and is not apologetic; one lives in association with householders, in inappropriate association with householders. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on these three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, eko ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, eko atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view. One is deficient in higher virtue, one is deficient in conduct, and one is deficient in view. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on these three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view.

‘‘Aparesampi, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya. Eko buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, eko saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati – imesaṃ kho, bhikkhave, tiṇṇaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ, ākaṅkhamāno saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissage, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kareyya.

Further, monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view. One speaks disparagingly of the Buddha, speaks disparagingly of the Dhamma, speaks disparagingly of the Saṅgha. Monks, if the Saṅgha wishes, it may impose the act of suspension on these three bhikkhus for not relinquishing a bad view.

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissage ukkhepanīyakamme

On the Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing a Bad View.

Ākaṅkhamānachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Sixes on Aspirations is concluded.

Tecattālīsavattaṃ

The forty-third section.

70. ‘‘Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakammakatena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā – na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo, na bhikkhunovādakasammuti sāditabbā, sammatenapi bhikkhuniyo na ovaditabbā. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti sā āpatti na āpajjitabbā, aññā vā tādisikā, tato vā pāpiṭṭhatarā; kammaṃ na garahitabbaṃ, kammikā na garahitabbā…pe… na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposatho ṭhapetabbo, na pavāraṇā ṭhapetabbā, na savacanīyaṃ kātabbaṃ, na anuvādo paṭṭhapetabbo, na okāso kāretabbo, na codetabbo, na sāretabbo, na bhikkhūhi sampayojetabba’’nti.

70.Monks, a monk against whom an act of suspension has been carried out for not relinquishing a wicked view should behave properly. And what is proper behavior in that case? He should not give ordination; he should not give dependence; he should not have a novice attend on him; he should not agree to the authorization to instruct nuns; even if authorized, he should not instruct nuns. The offense on account of which the Saṅgha carried out the act of suspension against him for not relinquishing a wicked view, that offense should not be committed, nor another offense like it, nor one worse than it. The act should not be disparaged; those who performed the act should not be disparaged… A monk in good standing’s Uposatha should not be stopped; his Pavāraṇā should not be stopped; he should not be addressed; no reproof should be initiated; no opportunity for confession should be made; he should not be accused; he should not be reminded; he should not associate with the monks.

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakamme

Concerning the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view.

Tecattālīsavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The forty-third section is concluded.

71. Atha kho saṅgho ariṭṭhassa bhikkhuno gaddhabādhipubbassa, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ akāsi – asambhogaṃ saṅghena. So saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato vibbhami. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma ariṭṭho bhikkhu gaddhabādhipubbo saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato vibbhamissatī’’ti? Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

71.Then the Saṅgha performed the act of suspension against the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture killer, for not relinquishing his wicked view—exclusion from association with the Saṅgha. Suspended by the Saṅgha for not relinquishing his wicked view, he went astray. The monks who were modest…pe… were critical, murmured, and expressed their dissatisfaction: “How could the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture killer, go astray after the Saṅgha performed the act of suspension against him for not relinquishing his wicked view?” Then those monks informed the Blessed One of this matter.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, ariṭṭho bhikkhu gaddhabādhipubbo saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato vibbhamatī’’ti [vibbhamīti (sī. ka.)]? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ…pe… kathañhi nāma so, bhikkhave, moghapuriso saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato vibbhamissati? Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetu.

Then the Blessed One, in connection with this cause, on this occasion, convened the Saṅgha of monks and questioned the monks: “Is it true, monks, that the monk Ariṭṭha, formerly a vulture killer, having been suspended by the Saṅgha for not relinquishing a wicked view, is going astray?” “It is true, Blessed One.” The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked him: “It is unseemly… How could that foolish man, monks, having been suspended by the Saṅgha for not relinquishing a wicked view, go astray? This will not lead to confidence in the unconvinced… Having rebuked him… after delivering a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: “Well then, monks, let the Saṅgha rescind the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view.”

Nappaṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-Third: On Not Rescinding

72. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Upasampādeti, nissayaṃ deti, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissage, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

72.“Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded. He gives ordination, he gives dependence, he attends to a novice, he accepts the appointment as an instructor of nuns, and even though appointed, he instructs nuns. Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded.”

[pari. 420] ‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ garahati, kammike garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ…pe….

“Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with five other factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded. He commits the offense for which the Saṅgha performed the act of suspension on account of his not relinquishing a wrong view, or another similar to it, or one worse than that. He disparages the act, he disparages those who performed it. Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with these five factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded….”

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, savacanīyaṃ karoti, anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, okāsaṃ kāreti, codeti, sāreti, bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ nappaṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

“Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with eight factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded. He prevents a regular bhikkhu from observing the Uposatha, he prevents him from performing the Pavāraṇā, he makes him subject to admonition, he establishes an accusation, he makes him give an opportunity, he accuses him, he reminds him (of the offense), he associates him with bhikkhus. Monks, for a bhikkhu endowed with these eight factors, if he does not relinquish a wrong view, the act of suspension should not be rescinded.”

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakamme

On the Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing a Wrong View

Nappaṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-Third on Not Rescinding is completed.

Paṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ

The Forty-three on What Should Be Revoked.

73. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na upasampādeti, na nissayaṃ deti, na sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhāpeti, na bhikkhunovādakasammutiṃ sādiyati, sammatopi bhikkhuniyo na ovadati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ.

73.Monks, for a monk possessing five qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked. He does not grant ordination, he does not give dependence, he does not attend upon a novice monk, he does not approve the agreement to be an advisor to nuns, and even though appointed, he does not advise the nuns—monks, for a monk possessing these five qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Yāya āpattiyā saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ kataṃ hoti taṃ āpattiṃ na āpajjati, aññaṃ vā tādisikaṃ, tato vā pāpiṭṭhataraṃ; kammaṃ na garahati, kammike na garahati – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ…pe….

Again, monks, for a monk endowed with five qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked. He does not commit the offense for which the Sangha imposed the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view, nor another similar to it, nor one worse than that; he does not disparage the action, nor those who performed the action—monks, for a monk endowed with these five qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked…etc.

‘‘Aṭṭhahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Na pakatattassa bhikkhuno uposathaṃ ṭhapeti, na pavāraṇaṃ ṭhapeti, na savacanīyaṃ karoti, na anuvādaṃ paṭṭhapeti, na okāsaṃ kāreti, na codeti, na sāreti, na bhikkhūhi sampayojeti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, aṭṭhahaṅgehi samannāgatassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambhetabbaṃ’’.

Monks, for a monk possessing eight qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked. He does not stop a monk in good standing from observing the Uposatha, he does not stop the Pavāraṇā, he does not make himself amenable to instruction, he does not initiate an accusation, he does not ask for an opportunity, he does not rebuke, he does not remind, and he does not associate with the monks—monks, for a monk possessing these eight qualities, who does not relinquish a wicked view, the act of suspension should be revoked.

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakamme

The Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing a Wicked View.

Paṭippassambhetabbatecattālīsakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Forty-three on What Should Be Revoked is Completed.

74. ‘‘Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṭippassambhetabbaṃ. Tena, bhikkhave, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakatena bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā vuḍḍhānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattāmi, lomaṃ pātemi, netthāraṃ vattāmi, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbā. Tatiyampi yācitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

74.And, monks, it should be revoked in this way. A monk who has been subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view should approach the Sangha, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the senior monks, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined palms, and say this: ‘Venerable sirs, I have been rightly subjected by the Sangha to the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view. I behave properly, I shave my hair, I conduct myself so as to be led out of this situation, and I request the revocation of the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view.’ He should make the request a second time. He should make the request a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Sangha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk named so-and-so, against whom the Sangha has carried out the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view, is conducting himself properly, shaves his hair, conducts himself so as to be led out of this situation, and requests the revocation of the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view. If it is agreeable to the Sangha, may the Sangha revoke the act of suspension against the monk named so-and-so for not relinquishing a wicked view. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk named so-and-so, who was subjected to an act of suspension by the Sangha for not relinquishing a wicked view, is conducting himself properly. He shaves his hair, conducts himself so as to be led out of this situation, and requests the revocation of the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view. The Sangha revokes the act of suspension for the monk named so-and-so for not relinquishing a wicked view. If it is agreeable to the venerable ones that the act of suspension for the monk named so-and-so, for not relinquishing a wicked view, be revoked, let him be silent; if it is not agreeable, let him speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu saṅghena, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammakato sammā vattati, lomaṃ pāteti, netthāraṃ vattati, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhiṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ paṭippassambheti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyassa kammassa paṭippassaddhi, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the second time, I speak on this matter…etc.… For the third time, I speak on this matter—Venerable sirs, may the Sangha hear me. This monk named so-and-so, who was subjected to the act of suspension by the Sangha for not relinquishing a wicked view, is conducting himself properly. He shaves his hair, conducts himself so as to be led out of this situation, and requests the revocation of the act of suspension for not relinquishing a wicked view. The Sangha revokes the act of suspension for the monk named so-and-so for not relinquishing a wicked view. If it is agreeable to the venerable ones, let them remain silent; if it is not agreeable, let them speak.

‘‘Paṭippassaddhaṃ saṅghena itthannāmassa bhikkhuno, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge, ukkhepanīyakammaṃ. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The act of suspension against the monk named so-and-so, for not relinquishing a wicked view, has been revoked by the Sangha. It is agreeable to the Sangha, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

Pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhepanīyakammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ sattamaṃ.

The Act of Suspension for Not Relinquishing a Wicked View is Completed, the Seventh.

Kammakkhandhako paṭhamo.

The Kamma Section, the First.

Imamhi khandhake vatthū satta.

In this section, there are seven cases.

Tassuddānaṃ –

Its Summary:

Paṇḍulohitakā bhikkhū, sayaṃ bhaṇḍanakārakā;Tādise upasaṅkamma, ussahiṃsu ca bhaṇḍane.

The Paṇḍulohitaka monks, who themselves caused quarrels; Approaching such ones, they strove in quarreling.

Anuppannāpi jāyanti [anuppannāni jāyanti (sī. syā.)], uppannānipi vaḍḍhare [uppannāni pavaḍḍhare (sī.), uppannāpi pavaḍḍhanti (ka.)];Appicchā pesalā bhikkhū, ujjhāyanti padassato [parīsato (syā.), parassato (sī.)].

Even those not arisen arise, and those arisen increase; the monks of few wishes and amiable are displeased at the sight of the fault.

Saddhammaṭṭhitiko buddho, sayambhū aggapuggalo;Āṇāpesi tajjanīyakammaṃ sāvatthiyaṃ jino.

The Buddha, established in the True Dhamma, self-existent, supreme among persons; the Victor at Sāvatthī prescribed the act of censure.

Asammukhāppaṭipucchāppaṭiññāya katañca yaṃ;Anāpatti adesane, desitāya katañca yaṃ.

Without being face to face, without questioning, without avowal, and what was done; There is no offense in non-disclosure, and what was done after disclosure.

Acodetvā asāretvā, anāropetvā ca yaṃ kataṃ;Asammukhā adhammena, vaggena cāpi [vaggenāpi ca (sī. syā.)] yaṃ kataṃ.

Without rebuking, without reminding, without establishing (an offense), and what was done; Without being face to face, unlawfully, and what was done by a faction as well.

Appaṭipucchā adhammena, puna vaggena [vaggenāpi ca (sī. syā.)] yaṃ kataṃ;Appaṭiññāya adhammena, vaggena cāpi [vaggenāpi ca (sī. syā.)] yaṃ kataṃ.

Without questioning, unlawfully, again, what was done by a faction; Without avowal, unlawfully, and what was done by a faction as well.

Anāpatti [anāpattiyā (sī. syā.)] adhammena, vaggena

There is no offense through illegality or by a group.

Cāpi [vaggenāpi ca (sī. syā.)] yaṃ kataṃ.

And also what was done.

Adesanāgāminiyā, adhammavaggameva ca.

By not leading to disclosure, and by an unrighteous faction.

Desitāya adhammena, vaggenāpi tatheva ca;Acodetvā adhammena, vaggenāpi tatheva ca.

By disclosure, unlawfully, and likewise by a faction; Without rebuking, unlawfully, and likewise by a faction.

Asāretvā adhammena, vaggenāpi tatheva ca;Anāropetvā adhammena, vaggenāpi tatheva ca.

Without reminding, unlawfully, and likewise by a faction; Without establishing (an offense), unlawfully, and likewise by a faction.

Kaṇhavāranayeneva, sukkavāraṃ vijāniyā;Saṅgho ākaṅkhamāno ca yassa tajjaniyaṃ kare.

Just as by the dark method, one should understand the bright method; and the Sangha, if it wishes, may perform the act of censure against whom it wishes.

Bhaṇḍanaṃ bālo saṃsaṭṭho, adhisīle ajjhācāre;Atidiṭṭhivipannassa, saṅgho tajjaniyaṃ kare.

A fool, involved in quarrels, associated (with evil companions), regarding higher virtue and misconduct; For one fallen away through extreme views, the Sangha may perform the act of censure.

Buddhadhammassa saṅghassa, avaṇṇaṃ yo ca bhāsati;Tiṇṇannampi ca bhikkhūnaṃ, saṅgho tajjaniyaṃ kare.

One who speaks dispraise of the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Sangha; and for even three monks, the Sangha should perform the act of censure.

Bhaṇḍanaṃ kārako eko, bālo saṃsagganissito;Adhisīle ajjhācāre, tatheva atidiṭṭhiyā.

One who causes quarrels, a fool, reliant on association (with evil companions), in higher virtue, in misconduct, and likewise in extreme views.

Buddhadhammassa saṅghassa, avaṇṇaṃ yo ca bhāsati;Tajjanīyakammakato, evaṃ sammānuvattanā.

One who speaks dispraise of the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Sangha, having been subjected to the act of censure, thus is proper conduct.

Upasampadanissayā, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhanā;Ovādasammatenāpi, na kare tajjanīkato.

Not granting dependence for ordination, not attending to a novice, even if appointed to give advice—a censured one should not do these.

Nāpajje tañca āpattiṃ, tādisañca tato paraṃ;Kammañca kammike cāpi, na garahe tathāvidho.

He does not commit that offense, nor one similar to it after that; and being such, he does not disparage the action nor those who performed the action.

Uposathaṃ pavāraṇaṃ, pakatattassa naṭṭhape;Savacaniṃ [na savacaniyaṃ (sī. syā.)] anuvādo, okāso codanena ca.

He does not stop the Uposatha and Pavāraṇā of a monk in good standing; he does not make himself amenable to instruction, does not initiate an accusation, does not ask for an opportunity, and does not rebuke.

Sāraṇaṃ sampayogañca, na kareyya tathāvidho;Upasampadanissayā, sāmaṇeraṃ upaṭṭhanā.

He does not remind or associate (with monks); he does not grant dependence for ordination, nor attend to a novice.

Ovādasammatenāpi, pañcahaṅgehi [pañcaaṅgo (ka.)] na sammati;Tañcāpajjati āpattiṃ, tādisañca tato paraṃ.

Even if appointed to give advice, he does not conform to these five qualities; he commits that offense, and one similar to it after that.

Kammañca kammike cāpi, garahanto na sammati;Uposathaṃ pavāraṇaṃ, savacanīyā ca novādo.

And disparaging the action and those who performed it, he does not conform; he does not conform to Uposatha, Pavāraṇā, amenability to instruction, and not advising.

Okāso codanañceva, sāraṇā sampayojanā;Imehaṭṭhaṅgehi yo yutto, tajjanānupasammati.

Opportunity, rebuke, reminding, and association; one who is endowed with these eight qualities is not pacified by censure.

Kaṇhavāranayeneva, sukkavāraṃ vijāniyā;Bālo āpattibahulo, saṃsaṭṭhopi ca seyyaso.

Just as by the dark method, one should understand the bright method; a fool, full of offenses, even when associated, is worse.

Niyassakammaṃ sambuddho, āṇāpesi mahāmuni;Kīṭāgirismiṃ dve bhikkhū, assajipunabbasukā.

The Perfectly Enlightened One, the Great Sage, prescribed the act of dependence; He enjoined it at Kīṭāgiri for the two monks, Assaji and Punabbasuka.

Anācārañca vividhaṃ, ācariṃsu asaññatā;Pabbājanīyaṃ sambuddho, kammaṃ sāvatthiyaṃ jino;Macchikāsaṇḍe sudhammo, cittassāvāsiko ahu.

They engaged in various kinds of misconduct, unrestrained. The Perfectly Enlightened One, the Victor, prescribed the act of banishment in Sāvatthī. Sudhamma, the resident of Citta, was in Macchikāsaṇḍa.

Jātivādena khuṃseti, sudhammo cittupāsakaṃ;Paṭisāraṇīyakammaṃ, āṇāpesi tathāgato.

Sudhamma reviled Citta the lay follower with talk of birth; the Tathagata enjoined the act of reconciliation.

Kosambiyaṃ channaṃ bhikkhuṃ, nicchantāpattiṃ passituṃ;Adassane ukkhipituṃ, āṇāpesi jinuttamo.

At Kosambi, the Supreme Victor enjoined the suspension of the monk Channa for not acknowledging an offense he did not wish to confess.

Channo taṃyeva āpattiṃ, paṭikātuṃ na icchati;Ukkhepanāppaṭikamme, āṇāpesi vināyako.

Channa did not wish to make amends for that very offense; the Leader enjoined suspension for not making amends.

Pāpadiṭṭhi ariṭṭhassa, āsi aññāṇanissitā;Diṭṭhiyāppaṭinissagge [diṭṭhiappaṭinissagge (ka.)], ukkhepaṃ jinabhāsitaṃ.

Ariṭṭha's wicked view was based on ignorance; for not relinquishing his view, the Victor prescribed suspension.

Niyassakammaṃ pabbajjaṃ [pabbājaṃ (ka.)], tatheva paṭisāraṇī;Adassanāppaṭikamme, anissagge ca diṭṭhiyā.

The act of dependence, expulsion, and likewise reconciliation; for non-acknowledgment (of offense), non-making-amends, and non-relinquishing of view.

Davānācārūpaghāti, micchāājīvameva ca;Pabbājanīyakammamhi, atirekapadā ime.

Violence, misconduct, harming, and wrong livelihood—these are additional terms in the act of expulsion.

Alābhāvaṇṇā dve pañca, dve pañcakāti nāmakā [dve pañcakoti nāmako (ka.)];Paṭisāraṇīyakammamhi, atirekapadā ime.

Dispraise of gain, two, five, two, and five by name—these are additional terms in the act of reconciliation.

Tajjanīyaṃ niyassañca, duve kammāpi sādisā [kammesu sadisaṃ (ka.)];Pabbajjā [pabbājā (ka.)] paṭisārī ca, atthi padātirittatā.

Censure and dependence, both acts are similar; expulsion and reconciliation, there is an excess of terms.

Tayo ukkhepanā kammā, sadisā te vibhattito;Tajjanīyanayenāpi, sesakammaṃ vijāniyāti.

The three acts of suspension are similar in their divisions; and by the method of censure, one should understand the remaining acts.

Kammakkhandhakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Kamma Section is Completed.
